 We owe you an explanation. 

December 5: An important update for readers in the United States. 

Please don't skip this 1-minute read. It's Friday, December 5, and this moment matters for Wikipedia because we haven't hit our goal yet. If you're like us, you've used Wikipedia countless times. To settle an argument with a friend. To satisfy a curiosity. Whether it's 3 in the morning or afternoon, Wikipedia is useful in your life. Please give $2.75.

After nearly 25 years, Wikipedia is still the internet we were promised‚Äîcreated by people, not by machines. It's not perfect, but it's not here to push a point of view. It's owned by a nonprofit, not a giant technology company or a billionaire.

Just 2% of our readers donate, so if you have given in the past and Wikipedia still provides you with $2.75 worth of knowledge, donate today. If you are undecided, remember any contribution helps.

25 years of the internet at its **best**

Where your donation goes

 Accountability and transparency are core values at the Wikimedia Foundation. We manage funds and resources to ensure that every contribution supports our mission. We have earned the Platinum Seal of Transparency from Candid (formerly GuideStar), and Charity Navigator awarded us its highest rating. You can [read our most recent annual report](https://annual.wikimedia.org/) for more information about our financial health. 

 Investment in Technology 45%
Nearly half of our budget goes toward supporting the technology that powers Wikipedia and other Wikimedia projects. We are constantly working to enhance the user experience for both contributors and readers, improve site security, and ensure reliable access to our websites globally. This infrastructure and product support sustain one of the top ten most visited websites in the world, all at a fraction of the cost of popular for-profit websites.

 Support for Volunteers 34%
The global reach of Wikimedia projects is made possible by the hard work of volunteers from across the globe. We provide grants, legal support, and other resources to help build vibrant volunteer communities. Additionally, we promote community engagement through outreach initiatives and advocate for the growth and protection of free knowledge.

 General and Administrative Expenses 12%
Operational costs are essential for the smooth management and governance of the Wikimedia Foundation. These expenses help us recruit top talent and support staff around the world, empowering them to carry out the mission of the Wikimedia Foundation.

 Allocation to Fundraising Efforts 11%
Donor support is crucial to sustaining Wikipedia and our other free knowledge endeavors. Our team is committed to efficient and effective fundraising throughout the year, ensuring that every contribution helps advance our mission.

[![Image 22](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4a/Commons-logo.svg/20px-Commons-logo.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Commons-logo.svg) Media related to [2022 FIFA World Cup](https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Category:2022_FIFA_World_Cup "commons:Category:2022 FIFA World Cup") at Wikimedia Commons

*   [e](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:EditPage/Template:2022_FIFA_World_Cup_sidebar "Special:EditPage/Template:2022 FIFA World Cup sidebar")

The **2022 FIFA World Cup** was the 22nd [FIFA World Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup "FIFA World Cup"), the quadrennial world championship for national [football](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Football "Football") teams organised by [FIFA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIFA "FIFA"). It took place in [Qatar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qatar "Qatar") from 20 November to 18 December 2022, after the country was awarded the hosting rights in 2010. It was the first World Cup to be held in the [Middle East](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_East "Middle East") and the [Arabian Peninsula](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula "Arabian Peninsula"), and the second in an Asian country after the [2002 tournament](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2002_FIFA_World_Cup "2002 FIFA World Cup") in [South Korea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Korea "South Korea") and [Japan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japan "Japan").[[A]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-2)

This tournament was the last with 32 participating teams, with the number of teams being increased to 48 for the [2026 World Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2026_FIFA_World_Cup "2026 FIFA World Cup"). To avoid the extremes of [Qatar's hot and humid climate in summers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geography_of_Qatar#Climate "Geography of Qatar"),[[2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-auto5-3) the event was held in November and December, becoming the first one to take place outside the traditional months of May, June, and July.[[2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-auto5-3)[[3]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-4) It was held over a reduced time frame of 29 days with 64 matches played in [eight venues](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#Stadiums) across [five cities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#Cities). [Qatar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qatar_national_football_team "Qatar national football team") entered the event‚Äîtheir first World Cup‚Äîautomatically as the host's national team, alongside 31 teams determined by the [qualification process](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification "2022 FIFA World Cup qualification").

[Morocco](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morocco_national_football_team "Morocco national football team") made history by becoming the first African nation to reach the semi-final of a World Cup, falling short 0‚Äì2 against [France](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/France_national_football_team "France national football team").[[4]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-5)[Argentina](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Argentina_national_football_team "Argentina national football team") were crowned the champions after winning [the final](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_final "2022 FIFA World Cup final") against the [title holder](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_final "2018 FIFA World Cup final")[France](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/France_national_football_team "France national football team") 4‚Äì2 on penalties following a 3‚Äì3 draw after extra time. It was Argentina's third title and their first since [1986](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1986_FIFA_World_Cup "1986 FIFA World Cup"). Argentina were the first nation from outside of Europe to win the tournament since [2002](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2002_FIFA_World_Cup "2002 FIFA World Cup"). French player [Kylian Mbapp√©](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kylian_Mbapp%C3%A9 "Kylian Mbapp√©") became the first player to score a [hat-trick](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hat-trick "Hat-trick") in a World Cup final since [Geoff Hurst](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geoff_Hurst "Geoff Hurst") in the [1966 final](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1966_FIFA_World_Cup "1966 FIFA World Cup") and won the [Golden Boot](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup_Golden_Boot "FIFA World Cup Golden Boot") as he scored the most goals (eight) during the tournament. Mbapp√© also became the first player to score in two consecutive finals since [Vav√°](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vav%C3%A1 "Vav√°") of Brazil did the same in 1958 and 1962.

Argentine captain [Lionel Messi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lionel_Messi "Lionel Messi") was voted the tournament's best player, winning his second [Golden Ball](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup_Golden_Ball "FIFA World Cup Golden Ball"). The tournament has been considered exceptionally poetic as the capstone of his career, with the win fulfilling for some commentators a previously unmet criterion to be regarded as the greatest player of all time.[[5]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-NYT2022-6) Teammates [Emiliano Mart√≠nez](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emiliano_Mart%C3%ADnez "Emiliano Mart√≠nez") and [Enzo Fern√°ndez](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Enzo_Fern%C3%A1ndez "Enzo Fern√°ndez") won the [Golden Glove](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup_Golden_Glove "FIFA World Cup Golden Glove"), awarded to the tournament's best [goalkeeper](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Goalkeeper_(association_football) "Goalkeeper (association football)"), and the [Young Player Award](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup_Young_Player_Award "FIFA World Cup Young Player Award"), awarded to the tournament's best young player, respectively. With 172 goals, the tournament set a record for the highest number of goals scored in the 32-team format, with every participating team scoring at least one goal.

The choice to host the World Cup in Qatar [attracted significant criticism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_controversies "2022 FIFA World Cup controversies"), with concerns raised over the country's [treatment of migrant workers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_controversies#Human_rights_concern "2022 FIFA World Cup controversies"), [women](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#LGBT_and_women's_rights), and [members of the LGBTQ+ community](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Qatar "LGBT rights in Qatar"), as well as Qatar's climate, [lack of a strong football culture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_controversies#Qatari_football_record "2022 FIFA World Cup controversies"), scheduling changes, and allegations of bribery for hosting rights and [wider FIFA corruption](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2015_FIFA_corruption_case "2015 FIFA corruption case").[[B]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-15)

Format
------

The [FIFA World Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup "FIFA World Cup") is a professional football tournament held between national football teams, organised by [FIFA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIFA "FIFA").[[14]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-16)[[15]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-17) The tournament, held every four years, was [first played in 1930](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1930_FIFA_World_Cup "1930 FIFA World Cup") in Uruguay,[[16]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-foxsports.com-18) and has been contested by 32 teams since the [1998 event](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1998_FIFA_World_Cup "1998 FIFA World Cup").[[16]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-foxsports.com-18) The tournament was contested with eight [round-robin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Round-robin_tournament "Round-robin tournament") groups followed by a [knockout round](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Single-elimination_tournament "Single-elimination tournament") for 16 teams.[[17]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-19) The defending champions were [France](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/France_national_football_team "France national football team"), who defeated [Croatia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Croatia_national_football_team "Croatia national football team") 4‚Äì2 in the [2018 FIFA World Cup Final](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_Final "2018 FIFA World Cup Final").[[18]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-20)[[19]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-21) The event was scheduled to take place under a reduced length,[[20]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-22) from 20 November to 18 December in Qatar.[[21]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-23)[[22]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-auto6-24)[[23]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-25) Being held in Qatar, it was the first World Cup tournament to be held in the [Arab world](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_world "Arab world").[[24]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-26) Spectators were not required to follow most [COVID-19 restrictions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/COVID-19_restrictions "COVID-19 restrictions") such as social distancing, wearing masks, and negative tests.[[25]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-27)

### Schedule

Unlike previous FIFA World Cups, which are typically played in June and July, because of [Qatar's intense summer heat and often fairly high humidity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geography_of_Qatar#Climate "Geography of Qatar"),[[2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-auto5-3)[[22]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-auto6-24)[[26]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-28) the 2022 World Cup was played in November and December.[[6]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-Atlantic_2022-7)[[27]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-29) As a result, the World Cup was unusually staged in the middle of the seasons of many domestic association football leagues, which started in late July or August, including all of the major European leagues, which had been obliged to incorporate extended breaks into their domestic schedules to accommodate the World Cup. Major European competitions had scheduled their respective competitions group matches to be played before the World Cup, to avoid playing group matches the following year.[[28]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-30)

The match schedule was confirmed by FIFA on 15 July 2020.[[29]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-schedule_confirmed-31) The group stage was set to begin on 21 November, with four matches every day. Later, the schedule was tweaked by moving the Qatar vs Ecuador game to 20 November, after Qatar lobbied FIFA to allow their team to open the tournament.[[30]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-32)[[31]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-33)[[32]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-34) The final was played on 18 December 2022, [National Day](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Day_(Qatar) "National Day (Qatar)"), at [Lusail Stadium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lusail_Stadium "Lusail Stadium").[[29]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-schedule_confirmed-31)[[33]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-schedule-35) Unlike previous tournaments where the match venues and kick-off times for each fixture were set prior to the draw, the assignment of group fixtures for each matchday to a specific venue and kick-off time was only made after the final draw, with the teams of each specific fixture known. This was due to the close proximity of the venues, which allowed the organisers to optimise stadium allocation for spectators and kick-off times for television audiences.[[29]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-schedule_confirmed-31)

The matches for each group were allocated to the following stadiums:[[33]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-schedule-35)

*   Groups A, B, E, F: [Al Bayt Stadium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Bayt_Stadium "Al Bayt Stadium"), [Khalifa International Stadium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khalifa_International_Stadium "Khalifa International Stadium"), [Al Thumama Stadium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Thumama_Stadium "Al Thumama Stadium"), [Ahmad bin Ali Stadium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahmad_bin_Ali_Stadium "Ahmad bin Ali Stadium")
*   Groups C, D, G, H: [Lusail Stadium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lusail_Stadium "Lusail Stadium"), [Stadium 974](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stadium_974 "Stadium 974"), [Education City Stadium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Education_City_Stadium "Education City Stadium"), [Al Janoub Stadium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Janoub_Stadium "Al Janoub Stadium")

FIFA confirmed the group stage venue and kick-off times on 1 April 2022, following the draw.[[34]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-36)[[35]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-37)

### Prize money

In April 2022, FIFA announced the prizes for all participating nations. Each qualified team received $1.5 million before the competition to cover preparation costs with each team receiving at least $9 million in prize money. This edition's total prize pool was $440 million, $40 million greater than the prize pool of the [previous tournament](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup "2018 FIFA World Cup").[[36]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-38)

| Place | Teams | Amount (in millions) |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Per team | Total |
| Champions | 1 | $42 | $42 |
| Runners-up | 1 | $30 | $30 |
| Third place | 1 | $27 | $27 |
| Fourth place | 1 | $25 | $25 |
| 5th‚Äì8th place (quarter-finals) | 4 | $17 | $68 |
| 9th‚Äì16th place (round of 16) | 8 | $13 | $104 |
| 17th‚Äì32nd place (group stage) | 16 | $9 | $144 |
| Total | 32 | $440 |

### Rule changes

The tournament featured new [substitution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Substitute_(association_football) "Substitute (association football)") rules whereby teams could make up to five substitutions in normal time, and an additional substitution in [extra time](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Overtime_(sports)#Association_football "Overtime (sports)").[[37]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-39)[[38]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-40)[[39]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-41) In addition, it was the first World Cup to feature [concussion substitutions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Substitute_(association_football)#Concussion_substitute "Substitute (association football)"), whereby each team was permitted to use a maximum of one concussion substitute during a match. A concussion substitution did not count towards a team's quota of regular substitutions.[[40]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-42) Iranian goalkeeper [Alireza Beiranvand](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alireza_Beiranvand "Alireza Beiranvand") suffered a concussion in [his country's opening match against England](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_Group_B#England_vs_Iran "2022 FIFA World Cup Group B") and was replaced by [Hossein Hosseini](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hossein_Hosseini_(footballer,_born_1992) "Hossein Hosseini (footballer, born 1992)"). This was the first use of a dedicated concussion substitute during a World Cup.[[41]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-43)

Host selection
--------------

Main articles: [2018 and 2022 FIFA World Cup bids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2018_and_2022_FIFA_World_Cup_bids "2018 and 2022 FIFA World Cup bids") and [Qatar 2022 FIFA World Cup bid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qatar_2022_FIFA_World_Cup_bid "Qatar 2022 FIFA World Cup bid")

[![Image 23](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Rusia_entreg%C3%B3_el_relevo_de_la_antorcha_de_la_Copa_del_Mundo_a_Qatar.jpg/250px-Rusia_entreg%C3%B3_el_relevo_de_la_antorcha_de_la_Copa_del_Mundo_a_Qatar.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Rusia_entreg%C3%B3_el_relevo_de_la_antorcha_de_la_Copa_del_Mundo_a_Qatar.jpg)

Russian President [Vladimir Putin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Putin "Vladimir Putin") handing over the symbolic relay baton for the hosting rights of the 2022 FIFA World Cup to Qatar's Emir [Tamim bin Hamad Al Thani](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tamim_bin_Hamad_Al_Thani "Tamim bin Hamad Al Thani") in June 2018.

The [bidding procedure to host the 2018 and 2022 FIFA World Cups](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2018_and_2022_FIFA_World_Cup_bids "2018 and 2022 FIFA World Cup bids") began in January 2009. National associations had until 2 February 2009 to register interest.[[42]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-44) Initially, 11 bids were made for the [2018 FIFA World Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup "2018 FIFA World Cup"), but Mexico withdrew from proceedings,[[43]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-45)[[44]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-46) and [Indonesia's bid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indonesia_2022_FIFA_World_Cup_bid "Indonesia 2022 FIFA World Cup bid") was rejected by FIFA in February 2010 after the Indonesian Football Association failed to submit a letter of [Indonesian government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Government_of_Indonesia "Government of Indonesia") guarantee to support the bid.[[45]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-reject-47)

After [UEFA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UEFA "UEFA") were guaranteed to host the 2018 event, members of UEFA were no longer in contention to host in 2022.[[46]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-48) There were five bids remaining for the 2022 FIFA World Cup: Australia, Japan, Qatar, South Korea, and the United States. The 22-member [FIFA Executive Committee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIFA_Executive_Committee "FIFA Executive Committee") convened in [Z√ºrich](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Z%C3%BCrich "Z√ºrich"), Switzerland, on 2 December 2010 to vote to select the hosts of both tournaments.[[47]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-2018+2022_bids-49)[[48]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-50) Two FIFA executive committee members were suspended before the vote in relation to allegations of corruption regarding their votes.[[49]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-51) The decision to host the 2022 World Cup in Qatar, which was graded as having "high operational risk",[[50]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-52) generated criticism from media commentators.[[51]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-53) It was criticised by many as being part of the FIFA corruption scandals,[[52]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-54) which led to the [2015 FIFA corruption case](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2015_FIFA_corruption_case "2015 FIFA corruption case").

The voting patterns were as follows:[[53]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-55)

2022 FIFA bidding (majority 12 votes) | Bidders | Votes |
| --- | --- |
| Round 1 | Round 2 | Round 3 | Round 4 |
| **Qatar** | 11 | 10 | 11 | 14 |
| United States | 3 | 5 | 6 | 8 |
| South Korea | 4 | 5 | 5 | Eliminated |
| Japan | 3 | 2 | Eliminated |
| Australia | 1 | Eliminated |

### Cost of hosting the tournament

At an estimated cost of over $220 billion,[[54]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-56) it is the most expensive World Cup ever held to date; this figure is disputed by Qatari officials, including organising [CEO](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CEO "CEO") Nasser Al Khater, who said the true cost was $8 billion, and other figures related to overall infrastructure development since the World Cup was awarded to Qatar in 2010.[[55]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-57)

Venues
------

Further information: [List of football stadiums in Qatar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_football_stadiums_in_Qatar "List of football stadiums in Qatar")

[![Image 24](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Stade_de_Lusail_match_Brazil_vs_Serbia.jpg/250px-Stade_de_Lusail_match_Brazil_vs_Serbia.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Stade_de_Lusail_match_Brazil_vs_Serbia.jpg)

Seven of the eight venues, including [Lusail Stadium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lusail_Stadium "Lusail Stadium"), the venue for the final, were new stadiums built specifically for the 2022 FIFA World Cup. The eighth was heavily renovated.

The first five proposed venues for the World Cup were unveiled at the beginning of March 2010. Qatar intended that the stadiums should reflect its history and culture, and for the designs to meet the following terms of reference: legacy, comfort, accessibility, and sustainability.[[56]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-58) The stadiums were equipped with cooling systems that aim to reduce temperatures within the stadium by up to 20¬∞C (36¬∞F).[[57]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-auto32-59)[[58]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-auto8-60)

Their marketing included statements describing the stadiums as [zero waste](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zero_waste "Zero waste"), and the upper tiers of the stadiums will be disassembled after the World Cup and donated to countries with less developed sports infrastructure.[[57]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-auto32-59)[[58]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-auto8-60) Qatar aspired to be compliant and certified by the [Global Sustainability Assessment System](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_Sustainability_Assessment_System "Global Sustainability Assessment System") (GSAS) for all the World Cup stadiums. All of the five stadium projects launched were designed by German architect [Albert Speer & Partners](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Speer_Jr. "Albert Speer Jr.").[[59]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-61) The Al Bayt and Al Wakrah stadiums were the only indoor stadiums of the eight used.[[60]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-62)

[![Image 25](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_Qatar_0%E2%80%932_Ecuador_-_%2821%29.jpg/250px-2022_FIFA_World_Cup_Qatar_0%E2%80%932_Ecuador_-_%2821%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:2022_FIFA_World_Cup_Qatar_0%E2%80%932_Ecuador_-_(21).jpg)

Some venues, such as the 68,000-seat [Al Bayt Stadium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Bayt_Stadium "Al Bayt Stadium"), were planned to have their upper tiers of seating removed to reduce capacity after the tournament, however this is yet to happen.

In an April 2013 report by [Merrill Lynch](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Merrill_Lynch "Merrill Lynch"), the organisers in Qatar requested that FIFA approve a smaller number of stadiums due to the growing costs.[[61]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-63)[Bloomberg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bloomberg_News "Bloomberg News") said that Qatar wished to cut the number of venues to eight or nine from the twelve originally planned.[[62]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-64) By April 2017, FIFA had yet to finalise the number of stadiums Qatar must have readied in five years' time. Qatar's Supreme Committee for Delivery and Legacy (SC) said it expected there would be eight in and near [Doha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doha "Doha"), with the exception of Al Khor.[[63]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-65)[[64]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-66)

Eight stadiums in five Qatari cities were built or renovated for the FIFA World Cup. Between 2010 (when Qatar were announced as hosts) and 2022, seven of the eight stadiums were built (some in place of older, outdated venues) and the [Khalifa International Stadium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khalifa_International_Stadium "Khalifa International Stadium") was renovated for the tournament.

*   Al Khor: Al Bayt Stadium (new). The first piles were driven into the ground in 2014. On 30 November 2021 it hosted its first match.
*   Lusail: Lusail Stadium (new). The construction of the stadium was started on 11 April 2017. It was completed on 21 November 2021.
*   Al Rayyan: Ahmad bin Ali Stadium (new). The stadium was built on the demolished [former stadium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahmed_bin_Ali_Stadium_(original) "Ahmed bin Ali Stadium (original)") site. It was commissioned on 18 December 2020.
*   Al Rayyan: Education City Stadium (new). It was completed on 15 June 2020.
*   Al Rayyan: Khalifa International Stadium (heavily renovated). The largest stadium in the country at the time, it was closed for renovation in 2014. It was commissioned in May 2017.
*   Doha: Al Thumama Stadium (new). Construction was completed on 21 October 2021.
*   Doha: Stadium 974 (new). Construction commenced in 2018. It was completed on 30 November 2021 and had hosted some of the matches in 2021 FIFA Arab Cup.
*   Al Wakrah: Al Janoub Stadium (new). Construction officially started in 2014 and was completed on 16 May 2019.

Of these eight stadiums, all but two have since been either dismantled, or have been moderately or heavily modified. The [Stadium 974](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stadium_974 "Stadium 974") was supposed to be dismantled after the tournament; as of November 2024 however, this has not happened and the stadium has sat abandoned in its original site‚Äîthis stadium was the first planned temporary stadium ever used for a FIFA World Cup.[[65]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-67)[Lusail Stadium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lusail_Stadium "Lusail Stadium"), [Al Bayt Stadium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Bayt_Stadium "Al Bayt Stadium"), [Ahmad bin Ali Stadium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahmad_bin_Ali_Stadium "Ahmad bin Ali Stadium"), [Education City Stadium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Education_City_Stadium "Education City Stadium"), [Al Thumama Stadium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Thumama_Stadium "Al Thumama Stadium") and [Al Janoub Stadium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Janoub_Stadium "Al Janoub Stadium") will be moderately or heavily modified as reduce their capacity by half.[[66]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-68) The [Khalifa International Stadium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khalifa_International_Stadium "Khalifa International Stadium") (latter along with the [Stadium 974](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stadium_974 "Stadium 974")) are the only largely unmodified stadium that were used for this tournament.

### Team base camps

Base camps were used by the 32 national squads to stay and train before and during the World Cup tournament. In July 2022, FIFA announced the hotels and training sites for each participating team.[[83]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-85)[[84]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-86) This World Cup was the most compact since the inaugural edition [in 1930](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1930_FIFA_World_Cup "1930 FIFA World Cup"), with 24 of the 32 teams being within a 10 km radius of each other, and are concentrated within the [Doha Area](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doha_Metropolitan_Area "Doha Metropolitan Area"). It was the first Cup since 1930 in which players did not need to take flights to matches and could remain at the same training base throughout the entire tournament.[[85]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-campsa2-87)[[86]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-campsb2-88)

### Security

The Qatari government employed about 50,000 security personnel, including police departments and military forces. These personnel came from at least thirteen countries, including Poland, Germany, France, Kuwait, Jordan, Italy, Palestine, Spain, Pakistan (4,500 Army troops), Turkey (3,000 riot police personnel), USA, Saudi Arabia and the United Kingdom.[[87]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-EA2-89)[[88]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-:9b2-90)[[89]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-91)

### Qualification

Main article: [2022 FIFA World Cup qualification](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification "2022 FIFA World Cup qualification")

[![Image 91](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/2022_world_cup_qualification.svg/500px-2022_world_cup_qualification.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:2022_world_cup_qualification.svg)

Teams qualified

Teams failed to qualify

Teams withdrew or suspended

Not a FIFA member

FIFA's [six continental confederations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIFA_confederations "FIFA confederations") organised their own [qualifying competitions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup_qualification "FIFA World Cup qualification"). All 211 [FIFA member associations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_FIFA_member_associations "List of FIFA member associations") were eligible to enter qualification.

*   The [Qatari national team](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qatar_national_football_team "Qatar national football team"), as hosts, qualified automatically for the tournament. They still participated in the Asian qualifying stage as the first two rounds also acted as [qualification](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2023_AFC_Asian_Cup_qualification "2023 AFC Asian Cup qualification") for the [2023 AFC Asian Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2023_AFC_Asian_Cup "2023 AFC Asian Cup").[[90]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-92) Since Qatar reached the final stage as winners in their group, [Lebanon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lebanon_national_football_team "Lebanon national football team"), the fifth-best second place team, advanced instead.[[91]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-93) Qatar were the only team making their debut in the FIFA World Cup, becoming the first hosts to make their tournament debut since [Italy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italy_national_football_team "Italy national football team") in [1934](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1934_FIFA_World_Cup "1934 FIFA World Cup").
*   Of the 32 nations qualified to play at the 2022 FIFA World Cup, 24 countries competed at the previous tournament in 2018,[[92]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-94) including [France](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/France_national_football_team "France national football team"), the reigning [World Cup champions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_FIFA_World_Cup_finals "List of FIFA World Cup finals"),[[93]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-95) who qualified for the event through European qualification rather than automatically as champions.
*   The [Netherlands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Netherlands_national_football_team "Netherlands national football team"), [Ecuador](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ecuador_national_football_team "Ecuador national football team"), [Ghana](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ghana_national_football_team "Ghana national football team"), [Cameroon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cameroon_national_football_team "Cameroon national football team"), and the [United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_men%27s_national_soccer_team "United States men's national soccer team") returned to the tournament after missing the 2018 edition.
*   [Canada](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canada_men%27s_national_soccer_team "Canada men's national soccer team") returned after 36 years, their only prior appearance being in [1986](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1986_FIFA_World_Cup "1986 FIFA World Cup").[[94]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-96)
*   [Wales](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wales_national_football_team "Wales national football team") made their first appearance in 64 years, the longest-ever gap for any team; their only previous participation having been in [1958](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1958_FIFA_World_Cup "1958 FIFA World Cup").[[95]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-:7-97)
*   [Ghana](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ghana_national_football_team "Ghana national football team") were the lowest ranked team to qualify, ranked 61st.[[96]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-98)
*   [Italy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italy_national_football_team "Italy national football team"), four-time winners and [reigning European champions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2020_Final "UEFA Euro 2020 Final"), failed to qualify for a second successive World Cup for the first time in their history, losing in the [qualification play-off semi-finals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_%E2%80%93_UEFA_second_round#Semi-finals_3 "2022 FIFA World Cup qualification ‚Äì UEFA second round").[[97]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-99) The Italians were the only former champions and the highest ranked team in the [FIFA Men's World Rankings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIFA_Men%27s_World_Ranking "FIFA Men's World Ranking") that failed to qualify. Italy were also the fourth team to have failed to qualify for the upcoming World Cup after having won the previous [UEFA European Championship](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UEFA_European_Championship "UEFA European Championship"), following [Czechoslovakia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Czechoslovakia_national_football_team "Czechoslovakia national football team") in [1978](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1978_FIFA_World_Cup "1978 FIFA World Cup"), [Denmark](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Denmark_national_football_team "Denmark national football team") in [1994](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1994_FIFA_World_Cup "1994 FIFA World Cup"), and [Greece](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greece_national_football_team "Greece national football team") in [2006](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup "2006 FIFA World Cup").[[98]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-100)

#### Withdrawals

*   [Saint Lucia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saint_Lucia_national_football_team "Saint Lucia national football team") initially entered [CONCACAF qualification](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_%E2%80%93_CONCACAF_first_round#Group_E "2022 FIFA World Cup qualification ‚Äì CONCACAF first round") but withdrew from it before their first match.
*   [North Korea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Korea_national_football_team "North Korea national football team") withdrew from the [AFC qualifying round](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_%E2%80%93_AFC_second_round#Group_H "2022 FIFA World Cup qualification ‚Äì AFC second round") due to safety concerns related to the [COVID-19 pandemic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_Asia "COVID-19 pandemic in Asia").
*   Both [American Samoa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Samoa_national_football_team "American Samoa national football team") and [Samoa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samoa_national_football_team "Samoa national football team") withdrew before the [OFC qualification](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_(OFC) "2022 FIFA World Cup qualification (OFC)") draw due to travel restrictions following the pandemic.[[99]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-101)
*   [Tonga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tonga_national_football_team "Tonga national football team") withdrew after the [2022 Hunga Tonga‚ÄìHunga Ha'apai eruption and tsunami](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_Hunga_Tonga%E2%80%93Hunga_Ha%27apai_eruption_and_tsunami "2022 Hunga Tonga‚ÄìHunga Ha'apai eruption and tsunami").[[100]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-102)
*   Due to [COVID-19](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/COVID-19 "COVID-19") outbreaks in their squads, [Vanuatu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vanuatu_national_football_team "Vanuatu national football team") and [Cook Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cook_Islands_national_football_team "Cook Islands national football team") also withdrew because of the [travel restrictions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Travel_during_the_COVID-19_pandemic "Travel during the COVID-19 pandemic").[[101]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-103)[[102]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-104)
*   The previous World Cup hosts, [Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russia_national_football_team "Russia national football team"), were disqualified from competing due to the [Russian invasion of Ukraine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine "Russian invasion of Ukraine").[[103]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-105)

### Squads

Main article: [2022 FIFA World Cup squads](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_squads "2022 FIFA World Cup squads")

Before submitting their final squad for the tournament, teams named a provisional squad of up to 55 players. Teams were required to have their 55-player roster submitted to FIFA by 21 October.[[105]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-107) Teams were required to name their final squads by 13 November.[[106]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-108) In August 2022, FIFA increased the final squad size to 26 players from a total of 23 players at the [2018 World Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup "2018 FIFA World Cup").[[107]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-109) All teams had a total of 26 players in their final squads except for [France](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/France_national_football_team "France national football team") and [Iran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran_national_football_team "Iran national football team"), who chose 25 players.[[108]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-110)[[109]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-111)

### Draw

Main article: [2022 FIFA World Cup seeding](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_seeding "2022 FIFA World Cup seeding")

The final draw was held at the Doha Exhibition and Convention Center in [Doha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doha "Doha"), Qatar,[[110]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-112) on 1 April 2022,[[111]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-113) 19:00 [AST](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabia_Standard_Time "Arabia Standard Time"), prior to the completion of [qualification](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification "2022 FIFA World Cup qualification"). The two winners of the [inter-confederation play-offs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_(inter-confederation_play-offs) "2022 FIFA World Cup qualification (inter-confederation play-offs)") and the winner of the [Path A of the UEFA play-offs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_%E2%80%93_UEFA_second_round#Path_A "2022 FIFA World Cup qualification ‚Äì UEFA second round") were not known at the time of the draw.[[112]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-114) The draw was attended by 2,000 guests and was led by [Carli Lloyd](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carli_Lloyd "Carli Lloyd"), [Jermaine Jenas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jermaine_Jenas "Jermaine Jenas") and sports broadcaster Samantha Johnson, assisted by the likes of [Cafu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cafu "Cafu") (Brazil), [Lothar Matth√§us](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lothar_Matth%C3%A4us "Lothar Matth√§us") (Germany), [Adel Ahmed Malalla](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adel_Ahmed_Malalla "Adel Ahmed Malalla") (Qatar), [Ali Daei](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ali_Daei "Ali Daei") (Iran), [Bora Milutinoviƒá](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bora_Milutinovi%C4%87 "Bora Milutinoviƒá") (Serbia/Mexico), [Jay-Jay Okocha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jay-Jay_Okocha "Jay-Jay Okocha") (Nigeria), [Rabah Madjer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rabah_Madjer "Rabah Madjer") (Algeria), and [Tim Cahill](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tim_Cahill "Tim Cahill") (Australia).[[113]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-drawProcedure-115)[[114]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-116)

For the draw, 32 teams were allocated into four pots based on the [FIFA Men's World Rankings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIFA_Men%27s_World_Rankings "FIFA Men's World Rankings") of 31 March 2022.[[115]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-117) Pot 1 contained host Qatar (who were automatically assigned to position A1) and the best seven teams. Pot 2 contained the next best eight teams, with the next best eight teams into pot 3. Pot 4 contained the five lowest-ranked teams, along with the placeholders for the two inter-confederation play-off winners and the UEFA Path A play-off winner. Teams from the same confederation could not be drawn into the same group except for UEFA teams, for which there was at least one and no more than two per group.[[116]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-auto2-118)

This principle also applied to the placeholder teams, with constraints applying based on the confederation of both potential winners of each play-off tie. The draw started with pot 1 and ended with pot 4, with each team selected then allocated into the first available group alphabetically. The position for the team within the group would then be drawn (for the purpose of the [match schedule](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#Schedule)), with the pot 1 teams automatically drawn into position 1 of each group.[[116]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-auto2-118) The pots for the draw are shown below.[[117]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-needtoknow-119)

#### Draw result

The eight groups were formed randomly, selecting one team from each of the four pots. Two teams from the same confederation could not be placed into the same group, with the exception of UEFA teams, where up to two teams could be in the same group. The only team whose position in the draw was predetermined was the host Qatar, who were placed into position A1.

Officiating
-----------

Main article: [2022 FIFA World Cup officials](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_officials "2022 FIFA World Cup officials")

In May 2022, FIFA announced the list of 36 referees, 69 assistant referees, and 24 [video assistant referees](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Video_assistant_referee "Video assistant referee") for the tournament. Of the 36 referees, FIFA included two each from Argentina, Brazil, England, and France.[[119]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-124)[[120]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-125)

For the first time women referees officiated games at a major men's tournament.[[121]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-126) France's [St√©phanie Frappart](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/St%C3%A9phanie_Frappart "St√©phanie Frappart"), [Salima Mukansanga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salima_Mukansanga "Salima Mukansanga") from Rwanda, and [Yoshimi Yamashita](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yoshimi_Yamashita "Yoshimi Yamashita") from Japan became the first female referees to be appointed to a men's World Cup.[[122]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-127) Frappart previously oversaw the [2019 FIFA Women's World Cup Final](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2019_FIFA_Women%27s_World_Cup_Final "2019 FIFA Women's World Cup Final").[[123]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-128) They were joined by three female assistant referees, Neuza Back, Kathryn Nesbitt, and Karen D√≠az Medina. Frappart then officially became the first-ever female referee to officiate a World Cup match when she worked the [Costa Rica vs Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_Group_E#Costa_Rica_vs_Germany "2022 FIFA World Cup Group E") match in [Group E](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_Group_E "2022 FIFA World Cup Group E") on 1 December.[[124]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-129)

Gambian referee [Bakary Gassama](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bakary_Gassama "Bakary Gassama") and Argentine assistant referee Juan Pablo Belatti were among the officials to serve at their third World Cup. Belatti was an assistant referee in the [2018 final](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_Final "2018 FIFA World Cup Final").[[125]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-130)[[126]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-131)[[127]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-132) Other returning officials included referees [C√©sar Arturo Ramos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/C%C3%A9sar_Arturo_Ramos "C√©sar Arturo Ramos") of Mexico and [Janny Sikazwe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Janny_Sikazwe "Janny Sikazwe") of Zambia, and Iranian assistant referee [Mohammadreza Mansouri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohammadreza_Mansouri "Mohammadreza Mansouri").[[128]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-133)[[129]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-134)[[130]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-135)

On 15 December 2022, FIFA announced that [Polish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_Football_Association "Polish Football Association") referee [Szymon Marciniak](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Szymon_Marciniak "Szymon Marciniak") would adjudicate the final.[[131]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-136)

Opening ceremony
----------------

Main article: [2022 FIFA World Cup opening ceremony](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_opening_ceremony "2022 FIFA World Cup opening ceremony")

The [opening ceremony](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_opening_ceremony "2022 FIFA World Cup opening ceremony") took place on Sunday, 20 November 2022 at the Al Bayt Stadium in Al Khor, prior to the [opening match of the tournament](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_Group_A#Qatar_vs_Ecuador "2022 FIFA World Cup Group A") between hosts Qatar and Ecuador.[[132]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-137) It included appearances by [Morgan Freeman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morgan_Freeman "Morgan Freeman") and [Ghanim Al-Muftah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ghanim_Al-Muftah "Ghanim Al-Muftah"), along with performances by South Korean singer and [BTS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BTS "BTS") member [Jungkook](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jungkook "Jungkook") and Qatari singer [Fahad Al Kubaisi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fahad_Al_Kubaisi "Fahad Al Kubaisi").[[133]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-138)[[134]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-139) It was the first time that the [Qur'an](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quran "Quran") had been recited as part of the opening ceremony.[[135]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-140) During the ceremony, [Emir](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emir_of_Qatar "Emir of Qatar")[Tamim bin Hamad Al Thani](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tamim_bin_Hamad_Al_Thani "Tamim bin Hamad Al Thani") declared the tournament open.[[136]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-141)

Group stage
-----------

[![Image 188](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Wc_2022_nd.png/250px-Wc_2022_nd.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Wc_2022_nd.png)

Result of countries participating in the 2022 FIFA World Cup

All times are local, [AST](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabia_Standard_Time "Arabia Standard Time") ([UTC+3](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UTC%2B03:00 "UTC+03:00")).

The group stage was played from 20 November to 2 December.[[137]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-142) Competing countries were divided into eight groups of four teams (groups A to H). Teams in each group played one another in a [round-robin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Round-robin_tournament "Round-robin tournament"), where the top two teams advanced to the [knockout stage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#Knockout_stage).

| show Tie-breaking criteria for group play |
| --- |
| The ranking of teams in the group stage was determined as follows:[[138]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-regulations-143) 1. Points obtained in all group matches; 2. Goal difference in all group matches; 3. Number of goals scored in all group matches; 4. Points obtained in the matches played between the teams in question; 5. Goal difference in the matches played between the teams in question; 6. Number of goals scored in the matches played between the teams in question; 7. Fair play points in all group matches (only one deduction could be applied to a player in a single match): * Yellow card: ‚àí1 points; * Indirect red card (second yellow card): ‚àí3 points; * Direct red card: ‚àí4 points; * Yellow card and direct red card: ‚àí5 points; 8. Drawing of lots. |
|  |

### Group A

Main article: [2022 FIFA World Cup Group A](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_Group_A "2022 FIFA World Cup Group A")

The first match of the tournament was held between Qatar and Ecuador in Group A. Ecuador had a disallowed goal in the opening minutes,[[139]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-144) but eventually won 2‚Äì0 with two goals from [Enner Valencia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Enner_Valencia "Enner Valencia").[[140]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-145) Qatar became the first host nation to lose their opening match at a World Cup.[[141]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-146)[[142]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-147)[[143]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-148) Many Qatar natives were seen leaving the game before the end, with [ESPN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ESPN "ESPN") reporting that two-thirds of the attendance had left.[[144]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-149)[[145]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-150) The other starting match in group A was won by the Netherlands 2‚Äì0 over Senegal. [Cody Gakpo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cody_Gakpo "Cody Gakpo") scored the opening goal in the 84th minute and [Davy Klaassen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Davy_Klaassen "Davy Klaassen") added a second in stoppage time.[[146]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-151) Senegal faced Qatar in the third match of the group; [Boulaye Dia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boulaye_Dia "Boulaye Dia") capitalised on a slip by [Boualem Khoukhi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boualem_Khoukhi "Boualem Khoukhi") to put Senegal 1‚Äì0 ahead. [Famara Di√©dhiou](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Famara_Di%C3%A9dhiou "Famara Di√©dhiou") scored a second with a header, before [Mohammed Muntari](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohammed_Muntari "Mohammed Muntari") scored Qatar's first-ever goal at a World Cup to reduce the deficit back to one. Senegal eventually won the match 3‚Äì1 after an 84th-minute goal by [Bamba Dieng](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bamba_Dieng "Bamba Dieng"). With this result, Qatar became the first team to be eliminated from the tournament, as well as becoming the first host nation to ever be knocked out of the tournament after two games.[[147]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-152) Gakpo scored his second goal of the tournament as the Netherlands led Ecuador; however, Valencia scored an equaliser in the 49th minute.[[148]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-153) The Netherlands won 2‚Äì0 against Qatar following goals by Gakpo and [Frenkie de Jong](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frenkie_de_Jong "Frenkie de Jong") to win the group, while Qatar attained the distinction of being the first home nation to lose all three group matches.[[149]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-154) Senegal faced Ecuador to determine the second knockout round qualifier. At the end of the first half, [Isma√Øla Sarr](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isma%C3%AFla_Sarr "Isma√Øla Sarr") scored a penalty kick to put Senegal ahead. In the 67th minute, [Mois√©s Caicedo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mois%C3%A9s_Caicedo "Mois√©s Caicedo") scored an equaliser, but shortly after, [Kalidou Koulibaly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kalidou_Koulibaly "Kalidou Koulibaly") gave Senegal the victory. The win was enough to qualify Senegal as the runners-up of Group A.[[150]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-155)

[![Image 189](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_Qatar_0%E2%80%932_Ecuador_-_%283%29.jpg/250px-2022_FIFA_World_Cup_Qatar_0%E2%80%932_Ecuador_-_%283%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:2022_FIFA_World_Cup_Qatar_0%E2%80%932_Ecuador_-_(3).jpg)

### Group B

Main article: [2022 FIFA World Cup Group B](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_Group_B "2022 FIFA World Cup Group B")

England completed a 6‚Äì2 victory over Iran. Iranian keeper [Alireza Beiranvand](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alireza_Beiranvand "Alireza Beiranvand") was removed from the game for a suspected [concussion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Concussion "Concussion") before England scored three first-half goals.[[151]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-EngIrn-156)[Mehdi Taremi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mehdi_Taremi "Mehdi Taremi") scored in the second half after which England defender [Harry Maguire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Maguire "Harry Maguire") was also removed for a concussion.[[151]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-EngIrn-156)[Timothy Weah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timothy_Weah "Timothy Weah"), of the United States, scored a first-half goal against Wales; however, the match finished as a draw after a penalty kick was won and scored by [Gareth Bale](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gareth_Bale "Gareth Bale").[[152]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-157) Iran defeated Wales 2‚Äì0 following a red card to Welsh goalkeeper [Wayne Hennessey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wayne_Hennessey "Wayne Hennessey") after he committed a foul outside of his [penalty area](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Penalty_area "Penalty area"). Substitute [Rouzbeh Cheshmi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rouzbeh_Cheshmi "Rouzbeh Cheshmi") scored the first goal eight minutes into stoppage time, followed by [Ramin Rezaeian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ramin_Rezaeian "Ramin Rezaeian") scoring three minutes later.[[153]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-158) England and the United States played to a 0‚Äì0 draw, with only four shots on target between them, and one shot from Christian Pulisic hit the crossbar.[[154]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-159) England won the group following a 3‚Äì0 win over Wales with a goal by [Phil Foden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phil_Foden "Phil Foden") and two by [Marcus Rashford](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marcus_Rashford "Marcus Rashford").[[155]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-160) With the United States needing no less than a win to advance, [Christian Pulisic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christian_Pulisic "Christian Pulisic") scored the winning goal while colliding with the opposing goalkeeper as the United States defeated Iran 1‚Äì0 to qualify for the round of 16.[[156]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-161)

### Group C

Main article: [2022 FIFA World Cup Group C](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_Group_C "2022 FIFA World Cup Group C")

Argentina took an early lead against Saudi Arabia after [Lionel Messi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lionel_Messi "Lionel Messi") scored a penalty kick after ten minutes; however, second-half goals by [Saleh Al-Shehri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saleh_Al-Shehri "Saleh Al-Shehri") and [Salem Al-Dawsari](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salem_Al-Dawsari "Salem Al-Dawsari") won the match 2‚Äì1 for Saudi Arabia,[[157]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-162) a result the media considered one of the biggest upsets in the history of the event.[[158]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-163)[[159]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-164) The match between Mexico and Poland ended as a goalless 0‚Äì0 draw after [Guillermo Ochoa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guillermo_Ochoa "Guillermo Ochoa") saved [Robert Lewandowski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Lewandowski "Robert Lewandowski")'s penalty kick attempt.[[160]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-165) Lewandowski scored his first career World Cup goal in a 2‚Äì0 win over Saudi Arabia four days later.[[161]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-166)[[162]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-167) Argentina defeated Mexico 2‚Äì0, with Messi scoring the opener and later assisting teammate [Enzo Fern√°ndez](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Enzo_Fern%C3%A1ndez "Enzo Fern√°ndez") who scored his first international goal.[[163]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-168)[[164]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-169) Argentina won their last game against Poland with goals from [Alexis Mac Allister](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexis_Mac_Allister "Alexis Mac Allister") and [Juli√°n √Ålvarez](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Juli%C3%A1n_%C3%81lvarez "Juli√°n √Ålvarez"), which was enough to win the group;[[165]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-170) Poland qualified for the knockout stage on goal difference, thanks to Saudi Arabia scoring an injury-time consolation goal against Mexico in a match already lost.[[166]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-171)

### Group D

Main article: [2022 FIFA World Cup Group D](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_Group_D "2022 FIFA World Cup Group D")

The match between Denmark and Tunisia ended as a goalless draw; both teams had goals disallowed by offside calls.[[167]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-SKYDenTun-172) Danish midfielder [Christian Eriksen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christian_Eriksen "Christian Eriksen") made his first major international appearance since suffering a cardiac arrest at the [UEFA Euro 2020](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2020 "UEFA Euro 2020").[[167]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-SKYDenTun-172) Defending champions France went a goal behind to Australia, after a [Craig Goodwin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Craig_Goodwin "Craig Goodwin") goal within ten minutes. France, however, scored four goals, by [Adrien Rabiot](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adrien_Rabiot "Adrien Rabiot"), [Kylian Mbapp√©](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kylian_Mbapp%C3%A9 "Kylian Mbapp√©") and two by [Olivier Giroud](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Olivier_Giroud "Olivier Giroud") to win 4‚Äì1.[[168]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-GuardianFraAus-173) The goals tied Giroud with [Thierry Henry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thierry_Henry "Thierry Henry") as France's all-time top goalscorer.[[168]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-GuardianFraAus-173)[Mitchell Duke](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mitchell_Duke "Mitchell Duke") scored the only goal as Australia won against Tunisia. This was their first World Cup win since 2010.[[169]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-auto4-174)[[170]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-175) Mbapp√© scored a brace as France defeated Denmark 2‚Äì1. This was enough for France to qualify for the knockout round‚Äîthe first time since Brazil in 2006 that the defending champions progressed through the opening round.[[169]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-auto4-174)[[171]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-176)[Mathew Leckie](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathew_Leckie "Mathew Leckie") scored the only goal as Australia defeated Denmark 1‚Äì0, qualifying for the knockout round as runners-up with the win.[[172]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-177)[Wahbi Khazri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wahbi_Khazri "Wahbi Khazri") scored for Tunisia against France in the 58th minute. Although [Antoine Griezmann](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antoine_Griezmann "Antoine Griezmann") equalised in stoppage time it was overturned for offside. Tunisia finished third in the group, as they required a draw in the Denmark and Australia game.[[173]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-178)

[![Image 279](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_France_4%E2%80%931_Australia_-_%2811%29.jpg/250px-2022_FIFA_World_Cup_France_4%E2%80%931_Australia_-_%2811%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:2022_FIFA_World_Cup_France_4%E2%80%931_Australia_-_(11).jpg)

### Group E

Main article: [2022 FIFA World Cup Group E](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_Group_E "2022 FIFA World Cup Group E")

Group E began with Japan facing [2014 champions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup "2014 FIFA World Cup") Germany. After an early penalty kick was converted by Germany's [ƒ∞lkay G√ºndoƒüan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C4%B0lkay_G%C3%BCndo%C4%9Fan "ƒ∞lkay G√ºndoƒüan"), Japan scored two second-half goals by [Ritsu D≈çan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ritsu_D%C5%8Dan "Ritsu D≈çan") and [Takuma Asano](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Takuma_Asano "Takuma Asano") in a 2‚Äì1 win.[[174]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-179) In the second group match, Spain defeated Costa Rica 7‚Äì0. First-half goals by [Dani Olmo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dani_Olmo "Dani Olmo"), [Marco Asensio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marco_Asensio "Marco Asensio"), and [Ferran Torres](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ferran_Torres "Ferran Torres") were followed by goals by [Gavi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gavi_(footballer) "Gavi (footballer)"), [Carlos Soler](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carlos_Soler_(footballer) "Carlos Soler (footballer)"), [Alvaro Morata](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alvaro_Morata "Alvaro Morata"), and a second by Torres.[[175]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-180)[[176]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-181) This was the largest defeat in a World Cup since Portugal's victory over North Korea in the [2010 event](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup "2010 FIFA World Cup") by the same scoreline.[[177]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-182) Costa Rica defeated Japan 1‚Äì0, with [Keysher Fuller](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Keysher_Fuller "Keysher Fuller") scoring with Costa Rica's first shot on target of the tournament.[[178]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-183) Germany and Spain drew 1‚Äì1, with [√Ålvaro Morata](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C3%81lvaro_Morata "√Ålvaro Morata") scoring for Spain and [Niclas F√ºllkrug](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Niclas_F%C3%BCllkrug "Niclas F√ºllkrug") scoring for Germany.[[179]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-184)[[180]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-185)[[181]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-186) Morata scored the opening goal for Spain against Japan as they controlled the first half of the match.[[182]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-:10-187) Japan equalised on [Ritsu Doan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ritsu_Doan "Ritsu Doan") before a second goal by [Ao Tanaka](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ao_Tanaka "Ao Tanaka") was heavily investigated by VAR for the ball potentially being out of play.[[183]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-Bunshun.jp_interview_Josek-188) The goal was awarded, and Japan won the group following a 2‚Äì1 win. Disputes over the VAR's call was only settled when the [Associated Press](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Associated_Press "Associated Press") released an iconic [bird's eye](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bird%27s_eye_view "Bird's eye view") photo of the ball after the match.[[183]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-Bunshun.jp_interview_Josek-188)[Serge Gnabry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Serge_Gnabry "Serge Gnabry") scored on ten minutes for Germany against Costa Rica and they led until half-time. Germany required a win, and for Japan to not win their match, or for both teams to win their matches by a combined goal difference of at least 9 goals, to qualify. In the second half, goals by [Yeltsin Tejeda](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yeltsin_Tejeda "Yeltsin Tejeda") and [Juan Vargas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Juan_Pablo_Vargas "Juan Pablo Vargas") gave Costa Rica a 2‚Äì1 lead, which would have qualified them into the knockout stages ahead of Spain. Germany scored three further goals‚Äîtwo by [Kai Havertz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kai_Havertz "Kai Havertz") and a goal by [Niclas Fullkrug](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Niclas_Fullkrug "Niclas Fullkrug"), ending in a 4‚Äì2 win for Germany‚Äîwhich was not enough to qualify them for the final stages. This was the second time in a row that the four-time champions failed to progress past the group stages.[[184]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-189) Japan won the group ahead of Spain.[[185]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-190)

### Group F

Main article: [2022 FIFA World Cup Group F](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_Group_F "2022 FIFA World Cup Group F")

Group F's first match was a goalless draw between Morocco and Croatia.[[186]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-191) Canada had a penalty kick in the first half of their match against Belgium which was saved by [Thibaut Courtois](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thibaut_Courtois "Thibaut Courtois"). Belgium won the match by a single goal by [Michy Batshuayi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michy_Batshuayi "Michy Batshuayi").[[187]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-192)[[188]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-193) Belgium lost 2‚Äì0 to Morocco, despite Morocco having a long-range [direct free kick goal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_kick_(association_football) "Free kick (association football)") by [Hakim Ziyech](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hakim_Ziyech "Hakim Ziyech") overturned for an offside on another player in the lead up to the goal. Two second-half goals from [Zakaria Aboukhlal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zakaria_Aboukhlal "Zakaria Aboukhlal") and [Romain Sa√Øss](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romain_Sa%C3%AFss "Romain Sa√Øss") helped the Morocco win their first World Cup match since 1998.[[189]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-194)[[190]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-195) The match sparked riots in Belgium, with fires and fireworks being set off by residents.[[191]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-196)[Alphonso Davies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alphonso_Davies "Alphonso Davies") scored Canada's first World Cup goal to give Canada the lead over Croatia. Goals by [Marko Livaja](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marko_Livaja "Marko Livaja"), [Lovro Majer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lovro_Majer "Lovro Majer"), and two by [Andrej Kramariƒá](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andrej_Kramari%C4%87 "Andrej Kramariƒá") for Croatia completed a 4‚Äì1 victory.[[192]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-197) Morocco scored two early goals through [Hakim Ziyech](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hakim_Ziyech "Hakim Ziyech") and [Youssef En-Nesyri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Youssef_En-Nesyri "Youssef En-Nesyri") in their game against Canada and qualified following a 2‚Äì1 victory. Canada's only goal was an [own goal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Own_goal "Own goal") by [Nayef Aguerd](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nayef_Aguerd "Nayef Aguerd").[[193]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-198) Croatia and Belgium played a goalless draw which eliminated Belgium, whose team was ranked second in the world, from the tournament.[[194]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-199)

### Group G

Main article: [2022 FIFA World Cup Group G](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_Group_G "2022 FIFA World Cup Group G")

[Breel Embolo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Breel_Embolo "Breel Embolo") scored the only goal in Switzerland's 1‚Äì0 defeat of Cameroon.[[195]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-200)[Richarlison](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richarlison "Richarlison") scored two goals as Brazil won against Serbia, with star player [Neymar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neymar "Neymar") receiving an ankle injury.[[196]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-201) Cameroon's [Jean-Charles Castelletto](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jean-Charles_Castelletto "Jean-Charles Castelletto") scored the opening goal against Serbia, but they were quickly behind as Serbia scored three goals by [Strahinja Pavloviƒá](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Strahinja_Pavlovi%C4%87 "Strahinja Pavloviƒá"), [Sergej Milinkoviƒá-Saviƒá](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sergej_Milinkovi%C4%87-Savi%C4%87 "Sergej Milinkoviƒá-Saviƒá"), and [Aleksandar Mitroviƒá](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aleksandar_Mitrovi%C4%87 "Aleksandar Mitroviƒá") either side of half time. Cameroon, however, scored goals through [Vincent Aboubakar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vincent_Aboubakar "Vincent Aboubakar") and [Eric Maxim Choupo-Moting](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eric_Maxim_Choupo-Moting "Eric Maxim Choupo-Moting"), completing a 3‚Äì3 draw.[[197]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-202) An 83rd-minute winner by [Casemiro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Casemiro "Casemiro") for Brazil over Switzerland was enough for them to qualify for the knockout stage.[[198]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-203) Having already qualified, Brazil were unable to win their final group game, as they were defeated by Cameroon 1‚Äì0 following a goal by [Vincent Aboubakar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vincent_Aboubakar "Vincent Aboubakar"). Already having a [yellow card](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yellow_card_(soccer) "Yellow card (soccer)"), he was later sent off for removing his shirt in celebrating the goal.[[199]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-204) Cameroon, however, did not qualify, as Switzerland defeated Serbia 3‚Äì2.[[200]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-205)

### Group H

Main article: [2022 FIFA World Cup Group H](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_Group_H "2022 FIFA World Cup Group H")

Uruguay and South Korea played to a goalless draw.[[201]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-206) A goalless first half between Portugal and Ghana preceded a penalty converted by [Cristiano Ronaldo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cristiano_Ronaldo "Cristiano Ronaldo") to give Portugal the lead. In scoring the goal, Ronaldo became the first man to score in five World Cups. Ghana responded with a goal by [Andr√© Ayew](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Ayew "Andr√© Ayew") before goals by [Jo√£o F√©lix](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_F%C3%A9lix "Jo√£o F√©lix"), and [Rafael Le√£o](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rafael_Le%C3%A3o "Rafael Le√£o") by Portugal put them 3‚Äì1 ahead. [Osman Bukari](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osman_Bukari "Osman Bukari") scored in the 89th minute to trail by a single goal, while [I√±aki Williams](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/I%C3%B1aki_Williams "I√±aki Williams") had a chance to equalise for Ghana ten minutes into stoppage time, but slipped before shooting. The match finished 3‚Äì2 to Portugal.[[202]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-207) Ghanaian [Mohammed Salisu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohammed_Salisu "Mohammed Salisu") opened the scoring against South Korea, with [Mohammed Kudus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohammed_Kudus "Mohammed Kudus") following it up. In the second half, [Cho Gue-sung](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cho_Gue-sung "Cho Gue-sung") scored a brace for South Korea, levelling the score. Mohammed Kudus scored again in the 68th minute, winning the match 3‚Äì2 for Ghana.[[203]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-208) Portugal defeated Uruguay 2‚Äì0 with two goals from [Bruno Fernandes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bruno_Fernandes "Bruno Fernandes"), advancing them to the knockout stage.[[204]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-209) A controversial penalty decision was called late in the game, with a suspected handball from [Jos√© Mar√≠a Gim√©nez](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Gim%C3%A9nez "Jos√© Mar√≠a Gim√©nez").[[205]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-210)[[206]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-211) Portugal led South Korea through [Ricardo Horta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ricardo_Horta "Ricardo Horta") after 10 minutes. However, goals by [Kim Young-gwon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Young-gwon "Kim Young-gwon") and [Hwang Hee-chan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hwang_Hee-chan "Hwang Hee-chan") won the match 2‚Äì1 for South Korea.[[207]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-212)[Giorgian de Arrascaeta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Giorgian_de_Arrascaeta "Giorgian de Arrascaeta") scored two goals as Uruguay defeated Ghana 2‚Äì0.[[208]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-213) However, with South Korea winning, Uruguay required another goal to progress as they finished third on goals scored.[[209]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-214) Several Uruguay players left the pitch after the game surrounding the referees and followed them off the pitch.[[210]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-215)[[211]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-216)[[212]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-217)
