Knockout stage
--------------

Main article: [2022 FIFA World Cup knockout stage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_knockout_stage "2022 FIFA World Cup knockout stage")

In the knockout stage, if the scores were equal when normal playing time expired, [extra time](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Overtime_(Association_football) "Overtime (Association football)") was played for two periods of 15 minutes each. This was followed, if required, by a [penalty shoot-out](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Penalty_shoot-out_(association_football) "Penalty shoot-out (association football)") to determine the winners.[[138]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-regulations-143)

All times are local, [AST](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabia_Standard_Time "Arabia Standard Time") ([UTC+3](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UTC%2B03:00 "UTC+03:00")).

### Round of 16

The round of 16 was played from 3 to 7 December,[[33]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-schedule-35) which for the first time ever included teams from [the Americas and four other continents](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Continent#Number "Continent").[[213]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-218) Group A winners Netherlands scored goals through [Memphis Depay](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Memphis_Depay "Memphis Depay"), [Daley Blind](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daley_Blind "Daley Blind"), and [Denzel Dumfries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Denzel_Dumfries "Denzel Dumfries") as they defeated the United States 3‚Äì1, with [Haji Wright](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haji_Wright "Haji Wright") scoring for the United States.[[214]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-219) Messi scored his third of the tournament alongside [Juli√°n √Ålvarez](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Juli%C3%A1n_%C3%81lvarez_(footballer) "Juli√°n √Ålvarez (footballer)") to give Argentina a two-goal lead over Australia, and despite an Enzo Fern√°ndez own goal from a [Craig Goodwin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Craig_Goodwin "Craig Goodwin") shot, Argentina won 2‚Äì1.[[215]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-220)[Olivier Giroud](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Olivier_Giroud "Olivier Giroud")'s goal and Mbapp√©'s brace enabled France to have a 3‚Äì1 victory over Poland, with [Robert Lewandowski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Lewandowski "Robert Lewandowski") scoring the lone goal for Poland from a penalty.[[216]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-221) England beat Senegal 3‚Äì0, with goals coming from [Jordan Henderson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jordan_Henderson "Jordan Henderson"), [Harry Kane](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Kane "Harry Kane"), and [Bukayo Saka](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bukayo_Saka "Bukayo Saka").[[217]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-222)[Daizen Maeda](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daizen_Maeda "Daizen Maeda") scored for Japan against Croatia in the first half before a leveller from [Ivan Peri≈°iƒá](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ivan_Peri%C5%A1i%C4%87 "Ivan Peri≈°iƒá") in the second. Neither team could find the winner, with Croatia defeating Japan 3‚Äì1 in a [penalty shoot-out](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Penalty_shoot-out_(association_football) "Penalty shoot-out (association football)").[[218]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-223)[Vin√≠cius J√∫nior](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vin%C3%ADcius_J%C3%BAnior "Vin√≠cius J√∫nior"), [Neymar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neymar "Neymar"), [Richarlison](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richarlison "Richarlison"), and [Lucas Paquet√°](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lucas_Paquet%C3%A1 "Lucas Paquet√°") all scored for Brazil, but a volley from South Korean [Paik Seung-ho](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paik_Seung-ho "Paik Seung-ho") reduced the deficit to 4‚Äì1.[[219]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-224)[Pablo Sarabia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pablo_Sarabia "Pablo Sarabia") had the best chance for Spain to break the deadlock against Morocco in stoppage time after two goalless hours, but he hit the goalie's right-hand post after a shot from the left; Morocco won the match 3‚Äì0 on penalties.[[220]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-225) A [hat-trick](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hat-trick "Hat-trick") by [Gon√ßalo Ramos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gon%C3%A7alo_Ramos "Gon√ßalo Ramos") led Portugal to defeat Switzerland 6‚Äì1, with goals from Portugal's [Pepe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pepe_(footballer,_born_1983) "Pepe (footballer, born 1983)"), [Rapha√´l Guerreiro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rapha%C3%ABl_Guerreiro "Rapha√´l Guerreiro"), and [Rafael Le√£o](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rafael_Le%C3%A3o "Rafael Le√£o") and from Switzerland's [Manuel Akanji](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manuel_Akanji "Manuel Akanji").[[221]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-226)

### Quarter-finals

The quarter-finals were played on 9 and 10 December.[[33]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-schedule-35) Croatia and Brazil ended 0‚Äì0 after 90 minutes and went to extra time. Neymar scored for Brazil in the 15th minute of extra time. Croatia, however, equalised through [Bruno Petkoviƒá](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bruno_Petkovi%C4%87 "Bruno Petkoviƒá") in the second period of extra time. With the match tied, a penalty shootout decided the contest, with Croatia winning the shootout 4‚Äì2.[[222]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-227)[[223]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-228) In the second quarter-final match, [Nahuel Molina](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nahuel_Molina "Nahuel Molina") and Messi scored for Argentina before [Wout Weghorst](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wout_Weghorst "Wout Weghorst") equalised with two goals shortly before the end of the game. The match went to extra time and then penalties, where Argentina would go on to win 4‚Äì3.[[224]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-229) Morocco defeated Portugal 1‚Äì0, with [Youssef En-Nesyri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Youssef_En-Nesyri "Youssef En-Nesyri") scoring at the end of the first half. Morocco became the first African and the first Arab nation to advance as far as the semi-finals of the competition.[[225]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-230) Despite [Harry Kane](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Kane "Harry Kane") scoring a penalty for England, it was not enough to beat France, who won 2‚Äì1 by virtue of goals from [Aur√©lien Tchouam√©ni](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aur%C3%A9lien_Tchouam%C3%A9ni "Aur√©lien Tchouam√©ni") and [Olivier Giroud](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Olivier_Giroud "Olivier Giroud") and a late missed penalty by Kane, sending them to their second consecutive World Cup semi-final and becoming the first defending champions to reach this stage since Brazil in 1998.[[226]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-231)[[227]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-232)

### Semi-finals

The semi-finals were played on 13 and 14 December.[[33]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-schedule-35) Messi scored a penalty kick before [Juli√°n √Ålvarez](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Juli%C3%A1n_%C3%81lvarez_(footballer) "Juli√°n √Ålvarez (footballer)") scored twice to give Argentina a 3‚Äì0 victory over Croatia.[[228]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-233)[Th√©o Hernandez](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Th%C3%A9o_Hernandez "Th√©o Hernandez") scored after five minutes as France led Morocco for most of the game. [Randal Kolo Muani](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Randal_Kolo_Muani "Randal Kolo Muani") scored in the 78th minute to complete a 2‚Äì0 victory for France over Morocco as they reached their second consecutive final.[[229]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-234)

### Third place play-off

The third place play-off was played on 17 December. The two teams had played against each other in their [opening game in Group F](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_Group_F#Morocco_vs_Croatia "2022 FIFA World Cup Group F") which finished 0‚Äì0. [Jo≈°ko Gvardiol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jo%C5%A1ko_Gvardiol "Jo≈°ko Gvardiol") promptly scored for Croatia, with [Achraf Dari](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Achraf_Dari "Achraf Dari") equalising just 2 minutes later. [Mislav Or≈°iƒá](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mislav_Or%C5%A1i%C4%87 "Mislav Or≈°iƒá") scored the winner for Croatia as the match finished 2‚Äì1.[[230]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-235) Morocco earned 4th place, a record for the team and the best World Cup finish of any African or Arab nation.[[231]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-236)

### Final

Main article: [2022 FIFA World Cup final](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_final "2022 FIFA World Cup final")

The final was played on 18 December between Argentina and France. Both teams had won the event twice previously.[[232]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-final1-237) Early goals from Lionel Messi and [√Ångel Di Mar√≠a](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C3%81ngel_Di_Mar%C3%ADa "√Ångel Di Mar√≠a") gave Argentina, leading 2‚Äì0, a head start against the French.[[232]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-final1-237)[[233]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-final2-238) Despite substitutions in the first half, France did not record a shot until after the 70th minute but were energised by additional substitutions in the 71st. A few minutes later, France were awarded a penalty as [Randal Kolo Muani](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Randal_Kolo_Muani "Randal Kolo Muani") was brought down in the penalty area by [Nicol√°s Otamendi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nicol%C3%A1s_Otamendi "Nicol√°s Otamendi"). Mbapp√© scored the penalty and added a second goal less than two minutes later to equalise the scores.[[233]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-final2-238) With the score tied at two goals apiece, the match went to extra time. Messi scored his second goal in the 108th minute, once again giving Argentina the lead. However, Mbapp√© was awarded a second penalty in the 115th minute after his shot hit the arm of [Gonzalo Montiel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gonzalo_Montiel "Gonzalo Montiel"). Mbapp√© scored his third goal, becoming the second player ever to complete a [hat-trick](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hat-trick "Hat-trick") in the final of a World Cup after [Geoff Hurst](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geoff_Hurst "Geoff Hurst") for England in [1966](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1966_FIFA_World_Cup "1966 FIFA World Cup").[[233]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-final2-238) With the score tied at 3‚Äì3, the match was determined via a penalty shootout. Argentina won the final after scoring all of their penalties, winning 4‚Äì2.[[233]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-final2-238) This marked their third World Cup win and their first since [1986](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1986_FIFA_World_Cup "1986 FIFA World Cup"), and also the second team (after [Spain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spain_national_football_team "Spain national football team") in [2010](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup "2010 FIFA World Cup")) to win the tournament after having lost their opening game.[[233]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-final2-238)

### Goalscorers

Note: Goals scored in penalty shoot-outs are not counted towards players' goal counts or to match goal counts.

[![Image 580](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_France_4%E2%80%931_Australia_-_%287%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-2022_FIFA_World_Cup_France_4%E2%80%931_Australia_-_%287%29_%28cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:2022_FIFA_World_Cup_France_4%E2%80%931_Australia_-_(7)_(cropped).jpg)

France forward [Kylian Mbapp√©](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kylian_Mbapp%C3%A9 "Kylian Mbapp√©") won the [Golden Boot award](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup_Golden_Boot "FIFA World Cup Golden Boot") after scoring eight goals in the tournament, the most since [Ronaldo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ronaldo_(Brazilian_footballer) "Ronaldo (Brazilian footballer)") in [2002](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2002_FIFA_World_Cup "2002 FIFA World Cup").

There were 172 goals scored in 64 matches, for an average of 2.69 goals per match.

Two own goals were scored throughout the tournament.[[234]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-239)

This was the most goals ever scored at a FIFA World Cup.[[235]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-240)

### Discipline

A player is automatically suspended for the next match for the following offences:[[138]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-regulations-143)

*   Receiving a red card (red card suspensions may be extended for serious offences)
*   Receiving two yellow cards in two matches; yellow cards expire after the completion of the quarter-finals (yellow card suspensions are not carried forward to any other future international matches)

The following suspensions were served during the tournament:

Awards
------

[![Image 738](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Lionel-Messi-Argentina-2022-FIFA-World-Cup.jpg/250px-Lionel-Messi-Argentina-2022-FIFA-World-Cup.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Lionel-Messi-Argentina-2022-FIFA-World-Cup.jpg)

Argentina captain and forward [Lionel Messi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lionel_Messi "Lionel Messi") won the [Golden Ball award](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup_Golden_Ball "FIFA World Cup Golden Ball"), becoming the first player to win it twice.

The following [World Cup awards](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup_awards "FIFA World Cup awards") were given at the conclusion of the tournament: the [Golden Boot](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup_Golden_Boot "FIFA World Cup Golden Boot") (top scorer), [Golden Ball](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup_Golden_Ball "FIFA World Cup Golden Ball") (best overall player) and [Golden Glove](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup_Golden_Glove "FIFA World Cup Golden Glove") (best goalkeeper).[[248]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-253)

Additionally, FIFA.com shortlisted 10 goals for users to vote on as the tournament's best. The award was won by Brazil's [Richarlison](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richarlison "Richarlison") for his second goal in the [group stage match against Serbia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_Group_G#Brazil_vs_Serbia "2022 FIFA World Cup Group G").[[249]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-254)

Marketing
---------

### Branding

The official emblem was designed by Unlock Brands[[250]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-255) and unveiled in September 2019, during simultaneous events at the [Doha Tower](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doha_Tower "Doha Tower"), [Katara Cultural Village](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Katara_Cultural_Village "Katara Cultural Village") amphitheatre, [Msheireb Downtown Doha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Msheireb_Downtown_Doha "Msheireb Downtown Doha"), and [Zubarah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zubarah "Zubarah"). It is based on a [shawl](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shawl "Shawl") (reflecting upon the tournament's late-Autumn scheduling) and desert [dunes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dune "Dune"), and was shaped to resemble the [tournament trophy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup_Trophy "FIFA World Cup Trophy"), the [infinity symbol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Infinity_symbol "Infinity symbol"), and the number "8"‚Äîreflecting upon the "interconnected" event and the eight host stadiums. The typography of the emblem's [wordmark](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wordmark "Wordmark") incorporated [kashida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kashida "Kashida")‚Äîthe practice of elongating certain parts of characters in [Arabic script](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabic_script "Arabic script") to provide typographical emphasis.[[251]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-256)[[252]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-257)[[253]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-258)

H.E Ambassador Dr. Hend Al-Muftah, Permanent Representative of the State of Qatar to the United Nations Office at Geneva, explained to [WIPO Magazine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WIPO_Magazine "WIPO Magazine") that the tournament provided an opportunity to "promote our culture and showcase our signature hospitality in a multicultural environment", and highlighted that the country has [used sports to](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Politics_and_sports "Politics and sports") demonstrate its "commitment to sustainable development, social inclusion and the values of community and mutual respect among peoples from different cultures and nations."[[254]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-259)

### Merchandise

See also: [FIFA World Cup video games](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup_video_games "FIFA World Cup video games")

[Electronic Arts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electronic_Arts "Electronic Arts")' licensed video games _[FIFA Mobile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIFA\_Mobile "FIFA Mobile")_ and _[FIFA 23](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIFA\_23 "FIFA 23")_ (except on [Nintendo Switch](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nintendo_Switch "Nintendo Switch")) received free updates with tie-in content for the 2022 World Cup on 8 and 9 November 2022, respectively. The update for _FIFA 23_ added World Cup-themed tournament modes with all teams and two of the stadiums from the event, campaigns and World Cup-themed unlockable content for Ultimate Team mode, and real-time squad and fixture updates during the tournament.[[255]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-260)

On 24 August 2022, the [Panini Group](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Panini_Group "Panini Group") produced themed stickers and a [sticker album](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sticker_album "Sticker album") for a 14th consecutive World Cup. This year, rare cards with coloured borders were included and could be collected, [traded](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trading_cards "Trading cards"), or sold.[[256]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-261)

On 12 April 2022, [FIFA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIFA "FIFA") released an [over-the-top media service](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Over-the-top_media_service "Over-the-top media service") and app revolving around the World Cup called FIFA+, where fans could play games, predict matches, and compete with others.[[257]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-262)

### Broadcasting rights

Main article: [2022 FIFA World Cup broadcasting rights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_broadcasting_rights "2022 FIFA World Cup broadcasting rights")

In May 2022, Infantino projected that the 2022 FIFA World Cup could be the most-watched in its history, with a global audience of at least 5 billion. The 2018 tournament was seen by 3.57 billion across the tournament.[[258]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-263) The various controversies surrounding the World Cup in Qatar led to questions over how the tournament would be covered in the media, and whether they would be discussed or addressed during coverage.[[259]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-264)[[260]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-:1-265) The match between England and the United States in the group stage was seen by approximately 20 million viewers across both Fox and [Telemundo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Telemundo "Telemundo"), ranking among the highest-rated associated football broadcasts in the United States (behind a 2014 World Cup match that drew 24.7 million).[[261]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-266)[[262]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-267)

### Sponsorship

[![Image 748](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/A7-BEB_-_Qatar_Airways_%28FIFA_World_Cup_2022_Livery%29_-_Boeing_777-3DZER_-_43215_-_VGHS.jpg/250px-A7-BEB_-_Qatar_Airways_%28FIFA_World_Cup_2022_Livery%29_-_Boeing_777-3DZER_-_43215_-_VGHS.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:A7-BEB_-_Qatar_Airways_(FIFA_World_Cup_2022_Livery)_-_Boeing_777-3DZER_-_43215_-_VGHS.jpg)

[Qatar Airways](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qatar_Airways "Qatar Airways") was one of the [sponsors](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sponsor_(commercial) "Sponsor (commercial)") of FIFA World Cup 2022.

The sponsors of the 2022 World Cup are divided into seven categories: FIFA Partners, FIFA World Cup Sponsors and African and Middle Eastern, Asian, European, North American and South American supporters. This marks the first time a FIFA World Cup is sponsored by supporters from seven different regions.

Symbols
-------

### Mascot

Main article: [La'eeb](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/La%27eeb "La'eeb")

The tournament's [official mascot](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup_mascot "FIFA World Cup mascot") was unveiled on 1 April 2022, during the group stage draw. Its name is "La ºeeb" ([Arabic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabic_language "Arabic language"): ŸÑÿπŸäÿ®, [romanised](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romanization_of_Arabic "Romanization of Arabic"):_La øƒ´b_), which is an Arabic word meaning "super-skilled player". The official website of FIFA says: "La ºeeb will be known for his youthful spirit; spreading joy and confidence everywhere he goes", and the official backstory of the character, published there, claims that it comes from a parallel world where tournament mascots live, "a world where ideas and creativity form the basis of characters that live in the minds of everyone".[[294]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-299)

### Match balls

Main article: [Adidas Al Rihla](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adidas_Al_Rihla "Adidas Al Rihla")

[![Image 749](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Al-Rihla_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Al-Rihla_%28cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Al-Rihla_(cropped).jpg)

Adidas Al Rihla

[![Image 750](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Predio_Deportivo_Lionel_Andr%C3%A9s_Messi_-_BugWarp_04_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Predio_Deportivo_Lionel_Andr%C3%A9s_Messi_-_BugWarp_04_%28cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Predio_Deportivo_Lionel_Andr%C3%A9s_Messi_-_BugWarp_04_(cropped).jpg)

Adidas Al Hilm

The first official match ball, "[Adidas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adidas "Adidas") Al Rihla", was unveiled on 30 March 2022. It was mainly inspired by the culture, architecture, iconic boats and flag of Qatar. In Arabic, the word _Al-Rihla_ (ÿßŸÑŸíÿ±ŸêŸëÿ≠ŸíŸÑŸéÿ© _ar-ri·∏•la_) means "the journey". The ball was designed with sustainability as a priority, making it the first-ever official match ball created with water-based glues and inks. As "the game is getting faster" and "speeds up", the ball has internal electronic sensors, allowing detection of its speed and position, updated 500 times per second[[295]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-300) and it has to be charged before each game.[[296]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-301) Two of the match balls were sent and returned from space by FIFA and [Qatar Airways](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qatar_Airways "Qatar Airways") on a [SpaceX](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SpaceX "SpaceX")[falcon 9](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Falcon_9 "Falcon 9")[suborbital mission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sub-orbital_spaceflight "Sub-orbital spaceflight") for promoting the World Cup.[[297]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-302)

The match ball for the semi-finals, third place play-off and [final](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_final "2022 FIFA World Cup final") was announced on 11 December 2022. It is a variation of the Al Rihla named the "Adidas Al Hilm _"_ ([Arabic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabic_language "Arabic language"): ÿßŸÑÿ≠ŸÑŸÖ, [romanised](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romanization_of_Arabic "Romanization of Arabic"):_al-·∏•ulm_, [lit.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Literal_translation "Literal translation")''the dream'', a reference to "every nation's dream of lifting the FIFA World Cup").[[298]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-303) While the technical aspects of the ball are the same, the colour is different from the Al Rihla balls used in the group stages and preceding knockout games, with a _Gold Metallic_, maroon, _Collegiate Burgundy_, and red design,[[299]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-304) a reference to the [national colours](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flag_of_Qatar "Flag of Qatar") of host nation [Qatar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qatar "Qatar") and the golden colours shared by the Final's [venue](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lusail_Stadium "Lusail Stadium") and the [FIFA World Cup Trophy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup_Trophy "FIFA World Cup Trophy").[[300]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-2022-03-30-fifa-305)

### Music

See also: [FIFA World Cup Qatar 2022 Official Soundtrack](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup_Qatar_2022_Official_Soundtrack "FIFA World Cup Qatar 2022 Official Soundtrack") and [List of FIFA World Cup songs and anthems](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_FIFA_World_Cup_songs_and_anthems "List of FIFA World Cup songs and anthems")

For the first time, a multi-song FIFA World Cup official soundtrack has been released, instead of one official song.[[301]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-306) The first song of the album is "[Hayya Hayya (Better Together)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hayya_Hayya_(Better_Together) "Hayya Hayya (Better Together)")", performed by [Trinidad Cardona](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trinidad_Cardona "Trinidad Cardona"), [Davido](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Davido "Davido"), and AISHA, released on 1 April 2022 along with the music video.[[302]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-307) The second song is "Arhbo", performed by [Gims](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gims "Gims") and [Ozuna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ozuna "Ozuna"), released on 19 August 2022 along with the music video.[[303]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-308) The third song is "The World Is Yours to Take" performed by American rapper [Lil Baby](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lil_Baby "Lil Baby"), released on 23 September 2022 along with a music video.[[304]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-309) The fourth song is "Light The Sky" performed by [Nora Fatehi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nora_Fatehi "Nora Fatehi"), [Manal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manal_(singer) "Manal (singer)"), [Rahma Riad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rahma_Riad "Rahma Riad"), and [Balqees](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balqees_(singer) "Balqees (singer)"), composed by [RedOne](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/RedOne "RedOne") and released on 7 October 2022 along with the music video.[[305]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-310) A fifth song, "[Tukoh Taka](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tukoh_Taka "Tukoh Taka")", performed by [Nicki Minaj](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nicki_Minaj "Nicki Minaj"), [Maluma](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maluma "Maluma") and [Myriam Fares](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Myriam_Fares "Myriam Fares"), was released on 17 November 2022 along with the music video, serving as the official song of the [FIFA Fan Festival](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIFA_Fan_Festival "FIFA Fan Festival").[[306]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-311) The final song is "[Dreamers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dreamers_(Jungkook_song) "Dreamers (Jungkook song)")" by [Jungkook](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jungkook "Jungkook") of [BTS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BTS "BTS") released on 20 November 2022. It was performed with [Fahad Al-Kubaisi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fahad_Al-Kubaisi "Fahad Al-Kubaisi") during the tournament's opening ceremony.[[307]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-312)[[308]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-313)

Controversies
-------------

Main article: [List of 2022 FIFA World Cup controversies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_2022_FIFA_World_Cup_controversies "List of 2022 FIFA World Cup controversies")

Criticism of the 2022 FIFA World Cup focused on Qatar's [human-rights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_rights_in_Qatar "Human rights in Qatar") record,[[309]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-foreignpolicy3-314) namely their [treatment of migrant workers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_controversies#Human_rights_concern "2022 FIFA World Cup controversies"),[[309]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-foreignpolicy3-314) women, and [position on LGBT rights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Qatar "LGBT rights in Qatar"),[[310]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-JPost_2022-315) leading to allegations of [sportswashing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sportswashing "Sportswashing").[[F]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-319) Others cited Qatar's climate, lack of a strong football culture, and allegations of bribery for hosting rights and [wider FIFA corruption](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2015_FIFA_corruption_case "2015 FIFA corruption case").[[7]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-Reason_2022-8)[[314]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-Atlantic_20222-320)[Boycotts of the event](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_controversies#Boycotts "2022 FIFA World Cup controversies") were declared by several countries, clubs, and individual players,[[312]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-Dhaka_2022-317)[[313]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-Comercio_2022-318) with former FIFA president [Sepp Blatter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sepp_Blatter "Sepp Blatter") twice stating that giving Qatar hosting rights was a "mistake".[[315]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-321)[[316]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-322) The FIFA World Cup delivered record-breaking numbers of TV audiences across multiple markets.[[317]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-323) In June 2023, _[Le Point](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Le\_Point "Le Point")_ revealed that FIFA World Cup has raised great interest in the country despite "calls for a [boycott](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boycott "Boycott")". According to the study by _Arcom_, six out of ten French people followed at least one match.[[318]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-324)

### Host selection criticism

There have been allegations of bribery and corruption in the selection process involving FIFA's executive committee members.[[319]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-325) These allegations are being investigated by FIFA (see [¬ßBidding corruption allegations, 2014](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#Bidding_corruption_allegations,_2014), below). In May 2011, allegations of corruption within the FIFA senior officials raised questions over the legitimacy of the World Cup 2022 being held in Qatar. The accusations of corruption were made relating to how Qatar won the right to host the event. A FIFA internal investigation and report cleared Qatar of any violation, but chief investigator [Michael J. Garcia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_J._Garcia "Michael J. Garcia") described FIFA's report on his enquiry as containing "numerous materially incomplete and erroneous representations."[[320]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-326)

In May 2015, Swiss federal prosecutors [opened an investigation into corruption and money laundering](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2015_FIFA_corruption_case "2015 FIFA corruption case") related to the [2018 and 2022 World Cup bids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2018_and_2022_FIFA_World_Cup_bids "2018 and 2022 FIFA World Cup bids").[[321]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-327)[[322]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-328) In August 2018, former FIFA president [Sepp Blatter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sepp_Blatter "Sepp Blatter") claimed that Qatar had used "black ops", suggesting that the bid committee had cheated to win the hosting rights.[[323]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-329) Some investigations found that Qatar sought an edge in securing hosting by hiring a former [CIA officer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency "Central Intelligence Agency") turned private contractor, Kevin Chalker, to spy on rival bid teams and key football officials who picked the winner in 2010.[[324]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-330)

In September 2018, a delegation from al-Ghufran tribe lodged a complaint to FIFA's president to reject the establishment of the World Cup in Qatar unless its government restored the Qatari nationality to all those affected from the tribe and returned land allegedly stolen from them to build the sport facilities.[[325]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-331)

In September 2023 it was reported that court documents show a transfer of $300M dollars were sent top people who voted on the 2022 World Cup host.[[326]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-332)

Qatar faced strong criticism for the treatment of foreign workers involved in preparation for the World Cup, with [Amnesty International](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amnesty_International "Amnesty International") referring to "forced labour" and poor working conditions,[[327]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-333)[[328]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-334) while many migrant workers reported having to pay large "recruitment fees" to obtain employment.[[329]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-guardian-workers-pay-335)_[The Guardian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Guardian "The Guardian")_ newspaper reported that many workers were denied food and water, had their identity papers taken away from them, and that they were not paid on time or at all, making some of them in effect slaves. _The Guardian_ estimated that up to 4,000 workers could die from lax safety and other causes by the time the competition was held. Between 2015 and 2021, the [Qatari government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Government_of_Qatar "Government of Qatar") adopted new labour reforms to improve working conditions, including a minimum wage for all workers and the removal of the [kafala system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kafala_system "Kafala system"). Furthermore, in November 2017, the [International Labour Organization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Labour_Organization "International Labour Organization") concluded that no rights were violated and made the decision to close the complaint against Qatar regarding the alleged violation of migrant workers' rights.[[330]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-336) According to Amnesty International, however, living and working conditions of the foreign workers did not improve in the last years.[[331]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-337)

Qatar was the smallest nation by area ever to have been awarded a FIFA World Cup‚Äì the next smallest by area was Switzerland, host of the [1954 World Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1954_FIFA_World_Cup "1954 FIFA World Cup"), which was more than three times as large as Qatar and only needed to host 16 teams instead of 32. Qatar also became only the second country (not including Uruguay and Italy, hosts of the first two World Cups) to be awarded a FIFA World Cup despite having never qualified for a previous edition: Japan was awarded co-hosting rights of the [2002 World Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2002_FIFA_World_Cup "2002 FIFA World Cup") in 1996 without ever having qualified for the finals, although they qualified for the [1998 edition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1998_FIFA_World_Cup "1998 FIFA World Cup"). Of the eight stadiums used in the tournament, six were located in the [Doha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doha "Doha")[metropolitan area](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doha_Metropolitan_Area "Doha Metropolitan Area"), making it the first World Cup [since 1930](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1930_FIFA_World_Cup "1930 FIFA World Cup") in which most of the stadiums were in one city. While this decreased the distance that fans and players needed to commute, Qatar itself struggled to accommodate the numbers of arriving fans with its diminutive amount of space.[[332]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-338)

Due to Qatar's [laws on alcohol consumption](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_with_alcohol_prohibition "List of countries with alcohol prohibition"), World Cup organisers announced the creation of designated "sobering-up" zones as an alternative to wide-scale arrests of intoxicated fans during the World Cup.[[333]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-339) Qatar's World Cup chief executive of the Supreme Committee for Delivery and Legacy, Nasser Al Khater, stated that the purpose of the designated sobering-up areas was to ensure the fans' safety.[[334]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-340) If a fan was sent to the "sobering up" zone, they were permitted to leave when they could display clearheaded behaviour.[[335]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-341) Multiple news agencies described the controversy as a "cultural clash" between [social conservatism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_conservatism "Social conservatism") and [Islamic morality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morality_in_Islam "Morality in Islam") against the "norms" of [secular](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Secularity "Secularity") Western [liberal democracies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liberal_democracy "Liberal democracy").[[12]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-:0-13)[[336]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-:2-342)

A number of groups and media outlets expressed concern over the suitability of Qatar to host the event.[[337]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-343)[[338]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-guardian-344) Issues regarding from [human rights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_rights_in_Qatar "Human rights in Qatar"),[[9]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-foreignpolicy-10)[[310]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-JPost_2022-315) worker conditions, the rights of [LGBT fans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LGBT_community "LGBT community"),[[310]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-JPost_2022-315) and the [illegality of homosexuality in Qatar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Qatar "LGBT rights in Qatar").[[339]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-345)[[340]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-346)[[341]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-347) In December 2020, Qatar said [rainbow flags](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rainbow_flag_(LGBT) "Rainbow flag (LGBT)") would be allowed at the 2022 FIFA World Cup.[[342]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-348) Qatari officials initially stated that they would not prohibit the display of [pride flags](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pride_flag "Pride flag") at tournament venues, although the country still advised LGBT attendees to comply with the country's [modesty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modesty "Modesty") and avoid [public displays of affection](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Public_display_of_affection "Public display of affection").[[343]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-:3-349)[[344]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-:4-350) Hassan Abdulla al-Thawadi, chief executive of the country's World Cup bid, said that Qatar would permit [alcohol consumption](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alcohol_consumption "Alcohol consumption") during the event,[[345]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-351)[[346]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-sportsgrid-352) even though [drinking in public](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drinking_in_public "Drinking in public") was not permitted.[[347]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-353) There were plans to allow the sale of alcohol inside stadiums and at fan villages.[[348]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-BBC_Sport-354) Normally, the sale of alcohol is restricted to non-Muslim guests at selected luxury hotels only.[[349]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-wsj201201072-355) However, in the months preceding the tournament, the display of LGBT material and the sale of alcohol were banned.[[348]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-BBC_Sport-354)[[350]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-:5-356)[[351]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-:6-357)[[352]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-Financial_Times-358)[[353]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-Reuters2-359)

The climate conditions caused some to call hosting the tournament in Qatar infeasible, with initial plans for air-conditioned stadiums giving way to a potential date switch from summer to November and December.[[6]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-Atlantic_2022-7) In May 2014, [Sepp Blatter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sepp_Blatter "Sepp Blatter"), who was FIFA president at the time of the selection, remarked that awarding the World Cup to Qatar was a "mistake" because of the extreme heat.[[6]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-Atlantic_2022-7)[[354]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-360)[[355]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-361) While addressing delegates from African and Asian confederations, Blatter said allegations of corruption and some of the criticism, including those from sponsors, were "very much linked to racism and discrimination".[[356]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-362) The attendance figures at the matches also came under scrutiny as the reported crowd attendance was more than the stadium capacities despite games having visible empty seats.[[357]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-363)

Prior to the tournament, a reporter for Denmark's [TV 2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TV_2_(Denmark) "TV 2 (Denmark)") was threatened by security during a live report from the [Katara Cultural Village](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Katara_Cultural_Village "Katara Cultural Village"); the organising committee apologised, stating that they were "mistakenly interrupted".[[358]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-364)[Tony O'Donoghue](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tony_O%27Donoghue "Tony O'Donoghue") of Ireland's [RT√â](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/RT%C3%89 "RT√â") also accused Qatari police of interrupting him while filming.[[359]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-365)

[Phaedra Almajid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phaedra_Al-Majid "Phaedra Al-Majid"), a former media officer for Qatar's 2022 World Cup bid, has alleged that three African football officials were offered bribes to support Qatar's bid. In a Netflix documentary series "[FIFA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIFA "FIFA") Uncovered," Almajid claims that [Hassan Al Thawadi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hassan_Al-Thawadi "Hassan Al-Thawadi"), who led Qatar's bid, offered ‚Ç¨2.3 million each to [Issa Hayatou](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Issa_Hayatou "Issa Hayatou") of Cameroon, [Jacques Anouma](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jacques_Anouma "Jacques Anouma") of Ivory Coast, and [Amos Adamu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amos_Adamu "Amos Adamu") of Nigeria in exchange for their votes. Qatar was competing with Australia, Japan, South Korea and the US for their bid for the 2022 World Cup. The alleged offer was made during a meeting of African football federations in January 2010. Almajid states that the money was intended for the football federations, not as personal bribes. She initially disclosed these allegations anonymously to the [Sunday Times](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Sunday_Times "The Sunday Times") after being dismissed from her position, but later retracted her claims, citing threats from [Qatar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qatar "Qatar"). Al Thawadi has denied these allegations, calling them false and expressing disappointment at the situation. The controversy adds to the ongoing scrutiny surrounding Qatar's successful bid to host the 2022 World Cup.[[360]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-366)

### Targeted hacking campaigns against critics

On November 2, 2022, Swiss media outlet SRF Investigativ published an investigative piece about Qatar's elaborate and extensive espionage operation to secure the World Cup hosting rights. The operation, which was dubbed [Project Merciless](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Project_Merciless "Project Merciless"), involved hacking emails and phones of FIFA officials and critics of Qatar's corruption and [poor human rights record](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_rights_in_Qatar "Human rights in Qatar"). It also targeted their friends and family members to run smear campaigns and influence FIFA policy. Starting on January 5, 2012, a cyberattack targeted Peter Hargitay, a Zurich-based FIFA insider and consultant for Australia's 2022 World Cup bid. Hargitay and his son hired an expert who traced the hack to a server linked to Rajat Khare of the mercenary Indian hack-for-hire firm [Appin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Appin_(company) "Appin (company)").[[361]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-SRF-2022-11-02-367)[[362]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-ap-qatar-spy-on-fifa-368)[[363]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-io-rajat-khare-helping-qatar-369)[[364]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-st-buy-the-world-cup-370) In November 2022, a lower court in [Geneva](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geneva "Geneva") ordered the publication to provisionally remove Rajat Khare's name and photo from the article.[[365]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-rsf-appin-silencing-media-371) As a result, he is currently referred to as an entrepreneur, though his name still appears in a [Reuters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reuters "Reuters") article about his involvement in the hacking.[[366]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-reuters-special-report-appin-372)

On 5 November 2022, _[The Sunday Times](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Sunday\_Times "The Sunday Times")_ and the [Bureau of Investigative Journalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bureau_of_Investigative_Journalism "Bureau of Investigative Journalism") published an investigation reporting that a group from an Indian hacking company had compromised the email accounts of various politicians, reporters, and other prominent individuals that had been critical of Qatar's hosting of the World Cup. It was also reported that the group had been hired by Jonas Rey, private investigators based in Switzerland, which were in turn hired by Qatari officials.[[367]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-The_Bureau_of_Investigative_Journalism-373)

### Migrant workers

Main article: [Human rights issues involving the 2022 FIFA World Cup ¬ßMigrant workers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_rights_issues_involving_the_2022_FIFA_World_Cup#Migrant_workers "Human rights issues involving the 2022 FIFA World Cup")

There was criticism regarding the state of [human rights in Qatar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_rights_in_Qatar "Human rights in Qatar") and of the conditions of migrant workers brought in to build the required infrastructure, including indentured servitude and working conditions leading to deaths.[[371]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-377) On 23 October 2022, an article published by _[The Guardian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Guardian "The Guardian")_ included statements from migrants working on the event infrastructure. Surveying 1,000 workers, 86% of participants said that the labour changes had improved their lives and that better working conditions are negotiable.[[372]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-378) Legislation has also been proposed on the minimum wage, summertime worker safety, and the election of migrant worker representatives in businesses. Labour mobility is a result of changes to the [Kafala system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kafala_system "Kafala system").[[373]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-379)

According to [Sharan Burrow](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sharan_Burrow "Sharan Burrow"), general secretary of the International Trade Union Confederation, prior to the tournament, "the new Kafala system tranche of law will put an end to Kafala and establish a contemporary industrial relations system."[[374]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-380)

FIFA President [Gianni Infantino](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gianni_Infantino "Gianni Infantino") has defended Qatar's decision to host the tournament.[[375]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-381)_[The Economist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Economist "The Economist")_ has asserted that Qatar has a better human rights record than [Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russia "Russia") and [China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/China "China"), and that the country has received excessive criticism after being selected to host the event.[[376]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-382)

### Move to November and December

Owing to the [climate in Qatar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_of_Qatar "Climate of Qatar"), concerns were expressed over holding the World Cup in its traditional time frame of June and July.[[6]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-Atlantic_2022-7) In October 2013, a task force was commissioned to consider alternative dates and report after the [2014 FIFA World Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup "2014 FIFA World Cup") in Brazil.[[377]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-autogenerated4-383) On 24 February 2015, the FIFA Task Force proposed that the tournament be played from late November to late December 2022,[[378]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-fifa_task_force-384) to avoid the summer heat and also avoid clashing with the [2022 Winter Olympics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_Winter_Olympics "2022 Winter Olympics") in February, the [2022 Winter Paralympics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_Winter_Paralympics "2022 Winter Paralympics") in March and [Ramadan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ramadan "Ramadan") in April.[[379]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-385)[[380]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-386)

The notion of staging the tournament in November was controversial because it would interfere with the regular season schedules of some domestic leagues around the world. Commentators noted the clash with the Christian Christmas season was likely to cause disruption, while there was concern about how short the tournament was intended to be.[[381]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-387) FIFA executive committee member [Theo Zwanziger](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theo_Zwanziger "Theo Zwanziger") said that awarding the event to Qatar was a "blatant mistake".[[382]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-388)

[Frank Lowy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frank_Lowy "Frank Lowy"), chairman of [Football Federation Australia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Football_Federation_Australia "Football Federation Australia"), said that if the 2022 World Cup were moved to November and thus upset the schedule of the [A-League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/A-League "A-League"), they would seek compensation from FIFA.[[383]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-389)[Richard Scudamore](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Scudamore "Richard Scudamore"), chief executive of the [Premier League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Premier_League "Premier League"), stated that they would consider legal action against FIFA because a move would interfere with the Premier League's popular Christmas and New Year fixture programme.[[384]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-390) In 2015, FIFA confirmed that the final would be played in December.[[385]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-391) Critics condemned the Euro-centrism of these allegations, and questioned why global sporting events must be held within the traditional European summer season.[[386]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-392)

### Bidding corruption allegations, 2014

See also: [Garcia Report](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Garcia_Report "Garcia Report")

Some allegations were made over the role of former football official [Mohammed bin Hammam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohammed_bin_Hammam "Mohammed bin Hammam") played in securing the bid.[[387]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-393) A former employee of the Qatar bid team alleged that several African officials were paid $1.5 million by Qatar.[[388]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-394) She retracted her claims, but later said that she was coerced to do so by Qatari bid officials.[[389]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-395)[[390]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-396) In March 2014, it was discovered that former [CONCACAF](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CONCACAF "CONCACAF") president [Jack Warner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jack_Warner_(football_executive) "Jack Warner (football executive)") and his family were paid almost $2 million from a firm linked to Qatar's successful campaign.[[391]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-397)

_[The Sunday Times](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Sunday\_Times "The Sunday Times")_ published bribery allegations based on a leak of millions of secret documents.[[392]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-398) Five of FIFA's six primary sponsors, [Sony](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sony "Sony"), [Adidas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adidas "Adidas"), [Visa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Visa_Inc. "Visa Inc."), [Hyundai](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hyundai_Motor_Company "Hyundai Motor Company"), and [Coca-Cola](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coca-Cola "Coca-Cola"), called upon FIFA to investigate the claims.[[393]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-399)[[394]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-400)[Jim Boyce](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jim_Boyce_(football_administrator) "Jim Boyce (football administrator)"), vice-president of FIFA, stated he would support a re-vote to find a new host if the corruption allegations are proven.[[395]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-401)[[396]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-402) FIFA completed a lengthy investigation into these allegations and a report cleared Qatar of any wrongdoing. Despite the claims, the Qataris insisted that the corruption allegations were being driven by envy and mistrust while Blatter said it was fuelled by racism in the British media.[[397]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-403)[[398]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-404)

In the [2015 FIFA corruption case](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2015_FIFA_corruption_case "2015 FIFA corruption case"), Swiss officials, operating under information from the [United States Department of Justice](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Justice "United States Department of Justice"), arrested many senior FIFA officials in Z√ºrich and seized physical and electronic records from FIFA's main headquarters. The arrests continued in the United States, where several FIFA officers were arrested, and FIFA buildings were raided. The arrests were made on the information of at least a $150 million corruption and bribery scandal.[[399]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-405) From those arrested, $40 million was forfeited under guilty pleas.[[400]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-Justice_Dept-406) In 2022, the president of the El Salvador soccer association, Reynaldo Vasquez, was sentenced to 16 months in prison in connection to over $350,000 in bribes.[[401]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-407)

Following the corruption case, Phaedra Almajid, the former media officer for the Qatar bid team, claimed that the allegations would result in Qatar not hosting the World Cup.[[402]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-408) In an interview published on the same day, [Domenico Scala](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Domenico_Scala_(manager) "Domenico Scala (manager)"), the head of FIFA's Audit and Compliance Committee, stated that "should there be evidence that the awards to Qatar and Russia came only because of bought votes, then the awards could be cancelled."[[403]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-BBC_News-409)[[404]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-Owen_Gibson-410)

In 2014, FIFA appointed Michael Garcia as its independent ethics investigator to look into bribery allegations against Russia and Qatar. Garcia investigated all nine bids and eleven countries involved in the 2018 and 2022 bids.[[405]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-411) At the end of the investigation, Garcia submitted a 430-page report. The FIFA governing body then appointed a German judge, Hans Joachim Eckert, who reviewed and presented a 42-page summary of the report two months later. The report cleared Qatar and Russia of bribery allegations, stating that Qatar "pulled Aspire into the orbit of the bid in significant ways" but did not "compromise the integrity" of the overall bid process.[[406]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-BBC-412) Michael Garcia reacted almost immediately, stating that the report is "materially incomplete" and contains "erroneous representations of the facts and conclusions".[[406]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-BBC-412)

In 2017, a German journalist Peter Rossberg claimed to have obtained the report and wrote that it "does not provide proof that the 2018 or 2022 World Cup was bought" and stated that he would publish the full report. This forced FIFA to release the original report. The full report did not provide any evidence of corruption against the host of the 2022 World Cup but stated that bidders tested the rules of conduct to the limit.[[407]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-413)

### Russian participation

On 9 December 2019, the [World Anti-Doping Agency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Anti-Doping_Agency "World Anti-Doping Agency") (WADA) handed Russia a four-year ban from all major sporting events, after [RUSADA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Anti-Doping_Agency "Russian Anti-Doping Agency") was found non-compliant for handing over manipulated lab data to investigators.[[408]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-414) The [Russian national team](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russia_national_football_team "Russia national football team") were still permitted to enter qualification, as the ban only applied to the final tournament to decide the world champions. A team representing Russia, which used the [Russian flag](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flag_of_Russia "Flag of Russia") and [anthem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_anthem_of_Russia "National anthem of Russia"), could not participate under the WADA decision whilst the ban was active.[[409]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-415) The decision was appealed to the [Court of Arbitration for Sport](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Court_of_Arbitration_for_Sport "Court of Arbitration for Sport"),[[410]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-416) and on 17 December 2020, Russian teams were banned from competing at world championships organised or sanctioned by a WADA signatory until 16 December 2022, the day before the third place play-off.[[411]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-417)

After the [Russian invasion of Ukraine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine "Russian invasion of Ukraine"), Russia's participation was further thrown into doubt. On 24 February 2022, the three teams in Russia's [qualifying path](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_%E2%80%93_UEFA_second_round "2022 FIFA World Cup qualification ‚Äì UEFA second round")‚Äî[Czech Republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Czech_Republic_national_football_team "Czech Republic national football team"), [Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Poland_national_football_team "Poland national football team"), and [Sweden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sweden_men%27s_national_football_team "Sweden men's national football team")‚Äîannounced their unwillingness to play any matches in Russian territory.[[412]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-418) Poland and Sweden extended the boycott on 26 February to any qualifying games, and the Czech Republic made the same decision one day later.[[413]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-419)[[414]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-420)[[415]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-421)

On 27 February 2022, FIFA announced a number of sanctions impacting Russia's participation in international football. Russia was prohibited from hosting international competitions, and the national team was ordered to play all home matches [behind closed doors](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Behind_closed_doors_(sport) "Behind closed doors (sport)") in neutral countries. Under these sanctions, Russia would not be allowed to compete under the country's name, flag, or national anthem; similarly to the Russian athletes' participation in events such as the Olympics,[[416]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-422) the team would compete under the abbreviation of their national federation, the [Russian Football Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Football_Union "Russian Football Union") ("RFU"), rather than "Russia".[[417]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-423) The next day, FIFA decided to suspend Russia from international competitions "until further notice", including its participation in the 2022 FIFA World Cup.[[418]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-424)

### LGBT and women's rights

Main article: [LGBT issues at the 2022 FIFA World Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LGBT_issues_at_the_2022_FIFA_World_Cup "LGBT issues at the 2022 FIFA World Cup")

There are no [LGBT rights in Qatar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Qatar "LGBT rights in Qatar"), with homosexuality as well as campaigning for [LGBTQ+](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LGBTQ%2B "LGBTQ+") rights criminalised. As such, when Qatar was selected to host the 2022 FIFA World Cup, the choice to do so in a restrictive nation saw much criticism, with the security of fans,[[419]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-425) as well as the homophobic football chants of certain nations, were points of discussion.[[420]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-426) The main controversy came from a last-minute FIFA decision to hand out player punishments to European captains who had months earlier announced their intention to continue wearing rainbow-coloured armbands (which began in 2020) in support of anti-discrimination. Typically, kit violations incur a fine, which the teams had said they would pay; on the day of the first match involving one of the teams, FIFA reportedly told the teams that they would receive a yellow card at a minimum for wearing the armbands.[[421]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-Denmark_ready_to_lead_European_withdrawal_from_FIFA_over_armband_row-427) Qatari officials stated that all people are welcome as long as they follow the public display of affection laws which apply to everyone.[[422]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-428)[[423]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-429)

Security officials at stadiums also confiscated items of rainbow clothing and flags featuring rainbows.[[424]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-Qatar_insists_rainbow_colours_are_allowed_at_World_Cup_after_%E2%80%98localised_incidents%E2%80%99_|_The_Independent-430)[[425]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-CNN_11-28-2022-431) American journalist [Grant Wahl](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grant_Wahl "Grant Wahl") was briefly detained for wearing a t-shirt with a rainbow on it.[[426]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-432) Wahl reportedly received death threats for wearing the shirt, later dying at the stadium.[[427]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-433)[[428]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-434) Other journalists with Wahl at the time of his death have reported that he began fitting or experiencing a seizure, and called for help himself. They criticised the Qatar Supreme Committee for not providing [defibrillators](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Defibrillator "Defibrillator") in the stadium, as they had looked for one to try to help Wahl.[[429]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-435) In response, FIFA said that according to the ambulance service, a defibrillator was made available when paramedics later arrived on scene.[[430]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-436) An autopsy done on Wahl in [New York City](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_City "New York City") later revealed that Wahl died from an [aortic aneurysm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aortic_aneurysm "Aortic aneurysm") rupture.[[431]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-437)

Discrimination against women in Qatar was also criticised.[[432]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-FIFI_World_Cup_Qatar_Controversial_Host-438)[[433]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-439)[Women in Qatar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Women_in_Qatar "Women in Qatar") have few freedoms,[[432]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-FIFI_World_Cup_Qatar_Controversial_Host-438)[[434]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-440) as they must obtain permission from their male guardians to marry, study abroad on government scholarships, work in many government jobs, travel abroad, receive certain forms of reproductive health care, and act as the primary guardian of children, even if they are divorced.[[435]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-441)

Qatar attracted particular criticism for an incident where a Mexican employee of the World Cup Organizing Committee was accused of allegedly having [sex outside of marriage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zina "Zina"). The woman had previously reported rape, while the male claimed to have been in a relationship with her, after which the woman was investigated for extramarital sex. Women in Qatar face the possible penalty of [flagellation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flagellation "Flagellation") and a seven-year prison sentence if convicted for having sex outside of marriage. The criminal case was eventually dropped months after she was allowed to leave Qatar.[[436]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-442)

### Influence of Iran

[![Image 751](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Iran_national_team_fan_01.jpg/250px-Iran_national_team_fan_01.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Iran_national_team_fan_01.jpg)

An Iranian fan showing a banner with "[Woman, Life, Freedom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Woman,_Life,_Freedom "Woman, Life, Freedom")" slogan.

In November 2022, there were reports suggesting that the government of [Iran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran "Iran") were working with Qatari officials to suppress anti-government protests at the 2022 FIFA World Cup,[[437]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-auto7-443) in light of the [Mahsa Amini protests](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mahsa_Amini_protests "Mahsa Amini protests"). Leaked documents and audio clips suggested that Iranian government officials were in correspondence with Qatari authorities in order to handle possible protesters.[[438]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-444)

In November 2022, the Qatari government revoked the visas of journalists from a London-based Iranian news channel, [Iran International](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran_International "Iran International"), known for being critical of the regime, who were seeking to cover the World Cup.[[439]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-445) On 21 November 2022, during the first group stage match from Group B, between Iran and England, attempts were reportedly made by the stadium's security forces to block Iranian fans who wore clothing or carried items bearing slogans that were deemed unsympathetic to the Islamic government of Iran.[[440]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-446) These included t-shirts and signs with "[Woman, Life, Freedom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Woman,_Life,_Freedom "Woman, Life, Freedom")" embedded onto them, Iran's previous flags, or any slogans containing the name of [Mahsa Amini](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Death_of_Mahsa_Amini "Death of Mahsa Amini").[[441]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-447) This crackdown continued throughout all of Iran's matches at the World Cup.[[437]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-auto7-443) In addition to removing fans from stadiums, reports showed that officials tried to suppress any filming or photography of possible protests. In one case, Qatari police detained Danish TV presenter, Rasmus Tantholdt, for filming fans with "Woman, Life, Freedom" slogans, some of whom who had been earlier abused by a group of pro-government supporters.[[442]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-448)

### Treatment of Jewish and Israeli visitors

Qatar had previously promised to provide Jewish tourists with cooked [_kosher_ food](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kashrut "Kashrut") and public [Jewish prayer services](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prayer_in_Judaism "Prayer in Judaism") at the tournament. However, shortly before the World Cup began, both were banned by Qatar, who claimed it could not secure the safety of Jews.[[443]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-449)[[444]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-450) Qatar alleged that they could not "secure" the safety of publicly praying Jewish tourists, whilst many foreign Jews complained that they subsequently had no food available to eat. It was estimated that 10,000 [religious Jews from Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_Jews "Israeli Jews") and around the world arrived to watch the World Cup in Qatar.[[445]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-:23-451)

Whilst Jewish organisations complained of being unable to find cooked kosher food,[[445]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-:23-451) the [Israeli government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Government_of_Israel "Government of Israel") said it was happy with the efforts made by Qatar to meet its requests, including kosher food, direct flights from Israel to Qatar, and temporary diplomatic representation in the country. A kosher kitchen under the supervision of Rabbi [Mendy Chitrik](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mendy_Chitrik "Mendy Chitrik") was open in time for the first match. Rabbi [Marc Schneier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marc_Schneier "Marc Schneier"), president of [The Foundation for Ethnic Understanding](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Foundation_for_Ethnic_Understanding "The Foundation for Ethnic Understanding"), said he had never asked the Qatari government for cooked food, and he had been the only person in communication with the Qataris regarding making the World Cup experience inclusive for Jews.[[446]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-452)

Multiple Israeli reporters at the tournament reported fans from [Arab nations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_world "Arab world") waving [Palestinian flags](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flag_of_Palestine "Flag of Palestine") and chanting [anti-Israeli](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Criticism_of_Israel "Criticism of Israel") slogans while harassing them.[[310]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-JPost_2022-315)[[447]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-merged1-453)[[448]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-454) Some Israelis reported that they had been escorted out of restaurants when their nationality was revealed.[[449]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-455) The Israeli government warned its citizens traveling to the tournament to hide their Israeli identity out of safety concerns.[[450]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-456)

### Accommodation

The [Rawdat Al Jahhaniya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rawdat_Al_Jahhaniya "Rawdat Al Jahhaniya") fan village was criticised for its overpriced "night cabins" (¬£185 per night) made out of shipping containers. Tourists complained that the air conditioners in the cabins did not function well, facilities were falling apart, and the sleeping experience did not match their expectations.[[451]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-457) The BBC reported that the tent accommodation at the Qetaifan Island fan village got criticism for having brown-coloured tap water and no air conditioning other than a standing fan.[[452]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-458)[[453]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-459) The tent village in [Al Khor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Khor "Al Khor") was criticised for having inconvenient transportation, a lack of alcohol, long waits to check in, and no locks on the tents.[[454]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-460)[[455]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-461) The lack of suitable and affordable accommodation raised demand for daily shuttle flights from neighbouring areas, such as Dubai, that had adequate numbers of hotel rooms.[[456]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup#cite_note-462)
